<p><span style="font-size: small;"><span id="coordinates"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_coordinate_system" title="Geographic coordinate system">Coordinates</a>: <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Malta&amp;params=35_53_N_14_30_E_region:MT_scale:300000"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">35°53′N</span> <span class="longitude">14°30′E</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">35.883°N 14.500°E</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">35.883; 14.500</span></span></span></a></span></span></span>
</p><p><b>Malta</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>, <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ɔː/: &#39;au&#39; in &#39;fraud&#39;">ɔː</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>-/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Malta.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/En-us-Malta.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Malta.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>; <small>Maltese:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Maltese" title="Help:IPA/Maltese">[ˈmɐltɐ]</a></span>), officially known as the <b>Republic of Malta</b> (<a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>: <i lang="mt">Repubblika ta' Malta</i>), is a Southern European <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> consisting of an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It lies 80&#160;km (50&#160;mi) south of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, 284&#160;km (176&#160;mi) east of <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ashby_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ashby-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and 333&#160;km (207&#160;mi) north of <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Malta is one of the world's smallest<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and most densely populated countries, at over 316&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (122&#160;sq&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-Zammit_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zammit-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> with a population of about 475,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Estimated_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estimated-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>, which is the smallest national capital in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> by area at 0.8&#160;km.<sup>2</sup> Its largest town is <a href="/wiki/Birkirkara" title="Birkirkara">Birkirkara</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> while its chief economic centre is <a href="/wiki/Sliema" title="Sliema">Sliema</a>. The official languages are <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a> and English, with Maltese also recognised as the national language. Maltese is the only <a href="/wiki/Semitic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Semitic language">Semitic language</a> to be officially recognised in the European Union. <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> is also spoken by most of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta has been inhabited since approximately 5900 BC. Its location in the centre of the Mediterranean<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> has historically given it great strategic importance as a naval base, with a succession of powers having contested and ruled the islands, including the Phoenicians, Carthaginians, Romans, Byzantines, Arabs, Normans, Sicilians, Spanish, <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights of St. John</a>, French, and British.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Most of these foreign influences have left some sort of mark on the country's ancient culture.
</p><p>Malta became a British colony in 1815, serving as a critical way station for ships and the headquarters for the British Mediterranean Fleet. It played an important role in the Allied war effort during the Second World War, and was subsequently <a href="/wiki/Award_of_the_George_Cross_to_Malta" title="Award of the George Cross to Malta">awarded the George Cross</a> for its bravery in the face of an <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">Axis siege</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and the George Cross appears on Malta's national flag.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The British Parliament passed the Malta Independence Act in 1964, giving Malta independence from the United Kingdom as the State of Malta, with Queen Elizabeth II as its head of state and queen.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The country became a republic in 1974. It has been a member state of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since independence, and joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in 2004; it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> monetary union in 2008.
</p><p>Malta has a long Christian legacy and its Archdiocese is claimed to be an <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_see" title="Apostolic see">apostolic see</a> because <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">Paul the Apostle</a> was shipwrecked on "Melita", according to <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_the_Apostles" title="Acts of the Apostles">Acts of the Apostles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> which is now widely taken to be Malta. Catholicism is the official religion in Malta. Article 40 of the Constitution states that "all persons in Malta shall have full freedom of conscience and enjoy the free exercise of their respective mode of religious worship."<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cia_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta is a popular tourist destination with its warm climate, numerous recreational areas, and architectural and historical monuments, including three UNESCO World Heritage Sites: <a href="/wiki/Hypogeum_of_%C4%A6al-Saflieni" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypogeum of Ħal-Saflieni">Hypogeum of Ħal-Saflieni</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and seven <a href="/wiki/Megalithic_Temples_of_Malta" title="Megalithic Temples of Malta">megalithic temples</a> which are some of the oldest free-standing structures in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-b1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The origin of the name <i>Malta</i> is uncertain, and the modern-day variation is derived from the Maltese language. The most common etymology is that the word <i>Malta</i> is derived from the Greek word <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">μέλι</span>, <i>meli</i>, "honey".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The ancient Greeks called the island <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Μελίτη</span> (<i>Melitē</i>) meaning "honey-sweet", possibly for Malta's unique production of honey; an endemic subspecies of <a href="/wiki/Maltese_honey_bee" title="Maltese honey bee">bee</a> lives on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Romans called the island <i>Melita</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> which can be considered either a latinisation of the Greek <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Μελίτη</span> or the adaptation of the Doric Greek pronunciation of the same word <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">Μελίτα</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another conjecture suggests that the word <i>Malta</i> comes from the Phoenician word <i>Maleth</i>, "a haven",<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> or 'port'<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> in reference to Malta's many bays and coves. Few other etymological mentions appear in classical literature, with the term <i>Malta</i> appearing in its present form in the <i><a href="/wiki/Antonine_Itinerary" title="Antonine Itinerary">Antonine Itinerary</a></i> (Itin. Marit. p.&#160;518; Sil. Ital. xiv. 251).<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Malta" title="History of Malta">History of Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Maltese_history" title="Timeline of Maltese history">Timeline of Maltese history</a></div>
<p>Malta has been inhabited from around 5900 BC,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> since the arrival of settlers from the island of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gozo_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gozo-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> A significant prehistoric <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> culture marked by <a href="/wiki/Megalithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Megalithic">Megalithic</a> structures, which date back to c. 3600 BC, existed on the islands, as evidenced by the temples of <a href="/wiki/Mnajdra" title="Mnajdra">Mnajdra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ggantija" class="mw-redirect" title="Ggantija">Ggantija</a> and others. The <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a> colonised Malta between 800–700 BC, bringing their <a href="/wiki/Semitic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Semitic language">Semitic language</a> and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> They used the islands as an outpost from which they expanded sea explorations and trade in the Mediterranean until their successors, the <a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a>, were ousted by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> in 216 BC with the help of the Maltese inhabitants, under whom Malta became a <a href="/wiki/Municipium" title="Municipium">municipium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.co.uk_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.co.uk-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After a period of <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine empire">Byzantine</a> rule (4th to 9th century) and a probable sack by the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> the islands were invaded by the <a href="/wiki/Aghlabids" title="Aghlabids">Aghlabids</a> in AD 870. The fate of the population after the Arab invasion is unclear but it seems the islands may have been completely depopulated and were likely to have been repopulated in the beginning of the second millennium by settlers from Arab-ruled Sicily who spoke <a href="/wiki/Siculo-Arabic" title="Siculo-Arabic">Siculo-Arabic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Muslim rule was ended by the <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Normans</a> who conquered the island in 1091. The islands were completely re-Christianised by 1249.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The islands were part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a> until 1530, and were briefly controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_House_of_Anjou" title="Capetian House of Anjou">Capetian House of Anjou</a>. In 1530 <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles I of Spain">Charles I of Spain</a> gave the Maltese islands to the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Order of Knights of the Hospital of St John of Jerusalem</a> in perpetual lease.
</p><p>The French under <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> took hold of the Maltese islands in 1798, although with the aid of the British the Maltese were able to oust French control two years later. The inhabitants subsequently asked Britain to assume sovereignty over the islands under the conditions laid out in a Declaration of Rights,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> stating that "his Majesty has no right to cede these Islands to any power...if he chooses to withdraw his protection, and abandon his sovereignty, the right of electing another sovereign, or of the governing of these Islands, belongs to us, the inhabitants and aborigines alone, and without control." As part of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1814)" title="Treaty of Paris (1814)">Treaty of Paris in 1814</a>, Malta became a British colony, ultimately rejecting an attempted integration with the United Kingdom in 1956.
</p><p>Malta became independent on 21 September 1964 (<a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Malta)" title="Independence Day (Malta)">Independence Day</a>). Under its 1964 constitution Malta initially retained Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Elizabeth II</a> as <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Malta" title="Queen of Malta">Queen of Malta</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor-General">Governor-General</a> exercising executive authority on her behalf. On 13 December 1974 (<a href="/wiki/Republic_Day_(Malta)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic Day (Malta)">Republic Day</a>) it became a republic within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Malta" title="President of Malta">President</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. On 31 March 1979 Malta saw the withdrawal of the last British troops and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> from Malta. This day is known as <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Day_(Malta)" title="Freedom Day (Malta)">Freedom Day</a> and Malta declared itself as a neutral and non-aligned state. Malta joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> on 1 May 2004 and joined the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> on 1 January 2008.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Megalithic_Temples_of_Malta" title="Megalithic Temples of Malta">Megalithic Temples of Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hypogeum_of_%C4%A6al-Saflieni" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypogeum of Ħal-Saflieni">Hypogeum of Ħal-Saflieni</a>, and <a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7ar_Dalam" title="Għar Dalam">Għar Dalam</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">Pottery</a> found by <a href="/wiki/Archaeologists" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeologists">archaeologists</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Skorba_Temples" title="Skorba Temples">Skorba Temples</a> resembles that found in Italy, and suggests that the Maltese islands were first settled in 5200 BCE mainly by <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> hunters or farmers who had arrived from the Italian island of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>, possibly the <a href="/wiki/Sicani" title="Sicani">Sicani</a>. The extinction of the <a href="/wiki/Hippopotamus_melitensis" title="Hippopotamus melitensis">dwarf hippos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palaeoloxodon_falconeri" title="Palaeoloxodon falconeri">dwarf elephants</a> has been linked to the earliest arrival of humans on Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Prehistoric farming settlements dating to the <a href="/wiki/Early_Neolithic" class="mw-redirect" title="Early Neolithic">Early Neolithic</a> period were discovered in open areas and also in caves, such as <a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7ar_Dalam" title="Għar Dalam">Għar Dalam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Skeates2010_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Skeates2010-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sicani" title="Sicani">Sicani</a> were the only tribe known to have inhabited the island at this time<sup id="cite_ref-gozo_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gozo-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and are generally regarded as being closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The population on Malta grew <a href="/wiki/Cereals" class="mw-redirect" title="Cereals">cereals</a>, raised livestock and, in common with other ancient Mediterranean cultures, worshiped a <a href="/wiki/Mother_goddess" title="Mother goddess">fertility figure</a> represented in Maltese prehistoric artefacts exhibiting the proportions seen in similar statuettes, including the <a href="/wiki/Venus_of_Willendorf" title="Venus of Willendorf">Venus of Willendorf</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ggantija_Temples,_Xaghra,_Gozo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ggantija_Temples%2C_Xaghra%2C_Gozo.jpg/220px-Ggantija_Temples%2C_Xaghra%2C_Gozo.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ggantija_Temples%2C_Xaghra%2C_Gozo.jpg/330px-Ggantija_Temples%2C_Xaghra%2C_Gozo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Ggantija_Temples%2C_Xaghra%2C_Gozo.jpg/440px-Ggantija_Temples%2C_Xaghra%2C_Gozo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3871" data-file-height="2581" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ggantija_Temples,_Xaghra,_Gozo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/%C4%A0gantija" title="Ġgantija">Ġgantija</a> <a href="/wiki/Megalith" title="Megalith">megalithic</a> temple complex</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_16_Mnajdra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Malta_16_Mnajdra.jpg/170px-Malta_16_Mnajdra.jpg" width="170" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Malta_16_Mnajdra.jpg/255px-Malta_16_Mnajdra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Malta_16_Mnajdra.jpg/340px-Malta_16_Mnajdra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4188" data-file-height="6096" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_16_Mnajdra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The temple complex of <a href="/wiki/Mnajdra" title="Mnajdra">Mnajdra</a></div></div></div>
<p>Pottery from the Għar Dalam phase is similar to pottery found in <a href="/wiki/Agrigento" title="Agrigento">Agrigento</a>, Sicily. A culture of <a href="/wiki/Megalith" title="Megalith">megalithis</a> temple builders then either supplanted or arose from this early period. Around the time of 3500 BCE, these people built some of the oldest existing free-standing structures in the world in the form of the megalithic <a href="/wiki/%C4%A0gantija" title="Ġgantija">Ġgantija</a> temples on <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-otsf_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-otsf-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> other early temples include those at <a href="/wiki/%C4%A6a%C4%A1ar_Qim" title="Ħaġar Qim">Ħaġar Qim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mnajdra" title="Mnajdra">Mnajdra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-b1_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-b1-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The temples have distinctive architecture, typically a complex trefoil design, and were used from 4000 to 2500 BCE. Animal bones and a knife found behind a removable altar stone suggest that temple rituals included <a href="/wiki/Animal_sacrifice" title="Animal sacrifice">animal sacrifice</a>. Tentative information suggests that the sacrifices were made to the goddess of fertility, whose statue is now in the National Museum of Archaeology in Valletta.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The culture apparently disappeared from the Maltese Islands around 2500 BCE. Archaeologists speculate that the temple builders fell victim to famine or disease, but this is not certain.
</p><p>Another archaeological feature of the Maltese Islands often attributed to these ancient builders is equidistant uniform grooves dubbed "cart tracks" or "cart ruts" which can be found in several locations throughout the islands, with the most prominent being those found in <a href="/wiki/Misra%C4%A7_G%C4%A7ar_il-Kbir" title="Misraħ Għar il-Kbir">Misraħ Għar il-Kbir</a>, which is informally known as "Clapham Junction". These may have been caused by wooden-wheeled carts eroding soft limestone.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After 2500 BCE, the Maltese Islands were depopulated for several decades until the arrival of a new influx of <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> immigrants, a culture that <a href="/wiki/Cremation" title="Cremation">cremated</a> its dead and introduced smaller megalithic structures called <a href="/wiki/Dolmen" title="Dolmen">dolmens</a> to Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In most cases there are small chambers here, with the cover made of a large slab placed on upright stones. They are claimed to belong to a population certainly different from that which built the previous megalithic temples. It is presumed the population arrived from <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> because of the similarity of Maltese dolmens to some small constructions found on the largest island of the Mediterranean sea.<sup id="cite_ref-Piccolo-dolmens_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Piccolo-dolmens-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Greeks.2C_Phoenicians.2C_Carthaginians_and_Romans"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Greeks,_Phoenicians,_Carthaginians_and_Romans">Greeks, Phoenicians, Carthaginians and Romans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Greeks, Phoenicians, Carthaginians and Romans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Magna_Graecia" title="Magna Graecia">Magna Graecia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cippi_of_Melqart" title="Cippi of Melqart">Cippi of Melqart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Ancient Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sicilia_(Roman_province)" title="Sicilia (Roman province)">Sicilia (Roman province)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a></div>
<p>Phoenician traders<sup id="cite_ref-ndmh_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ndmh-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> colonised the islands sometime after 1000 BCE<sup id="cite_ref-ashby_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ashby-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> as a stop on their trade routes from the eastern <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, joining the natives on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The Phoenicians inhabited the area now known as <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">Mdina</a>, and its surrounding town of <a href="/wiki/Rabat,_Malta" title="Rabat, Malta">Rabat</a>, which they called <i><a href="/wiki/Melite_(ancient_city)" title="Melite (ancient city)">Maleth</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cassar53–55_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cassar53–55-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, who also much later inhabited Mdina, referred to it (and the island) as <i>Melita</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roman_Malta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Roman_Malta.jpg/220px-Roman_Malta.jpg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Roman_Malta.jpg/330px-Roman_Malta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Roman_Malta.jpg/440px-Roman_Malta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="391" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roman_Malta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> mosaic from the <a href="/wiki/Domvs_Romana" title="Domvs Romana">Domvs Romana</a></div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Tyre_(332_BC)" title="Siege of Tyre (332 BC)">fall of Phoenicia</a> in 332 BCE, the area came under the control of <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a>, a former Phoenician colony.<sup id="cite_ref-ashby_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ashby-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-maltihist_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maltihist-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> During this time the people on Malta mainly cultivated <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceratonia_siliqua" title="Ceratonia siliqua">carob</a> and produced textiles.<sup id="cite_ref-maltihist_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maltihist-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/First_Punic_War" title="First Punic War">First Punic War</a>, the island was conquered after harsh fighting by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Atilius_Regulus" title="Marcus Atilius Regulus">Marcus Atilius Regulus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> After the failure of his expedition, the island fell back in the hands of Carthage, only to be conquered again in 218 BCE, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a>, by Roman Consul <a href="/wiki/Tiberius_Sempronius_Longus_(consul_218_BC)" title="Tiberius Sempronius Longus (consul 218 BC)">Tiberius Sempronius Longus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> After that, Malta became <i><a href="/wiki/Civitas" title="Civitas">Foederata Civitas</a></i>, a designation that meant it was exempt from paying <a href="/wiki/Tribute" title="Tribute">tribute</a> or the rule of <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a>, and fell within the jurisdiction of <a href="/wiki/Sicilia_(Roman_province)" title="Sicilia (Roman province)">the province of Sicily</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Punic influence, however, remained vibrant on the islands with the famous <a href="/wiki/Cippi_of_Melqart" title="Cippi of Melqart">Cippi of Melqart</a>, pivotal in deciphering the <a href="/wiki/Punic_language" title="Punic language">Punic language</a>, dedicated in the 2nd century BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Also the local Roman coinage, which ceased in the 1st century BCE,<sup id="cite_ref-cassar56–57_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cassar56–57-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> indicates the slow pace of the island's Romanization, since the very last locally minted coins still bear inscriptions in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> on the obverse (like "ΜΕΛΙΤΑΙΩ", meaning "of the Maltese") and Punic motifs, showing the resistance of the Greek and Punic cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Greeks settled in the Maltese islands beginning circa 700 BCE, as testified by several architectural remains, and remained throughout the Roman dominium.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> At around 160 BCE coins struck in Malta bore the Greek ‘ΜΕΛΙΤΑΙΩΝ’ (Melitaion) meaning ‘of the Maltese’. By 50 BCE Maltese coins had a Greek legend on one side and a Latin one on the other. Later coins were issued with just the Latin legend ‘MELITAS’. The depiction of aspects of the Punic religion, together with the use of the Greek alphabet, testifies to the resilience of Punic and Greek culture in Malta long after the arrival of the Romans.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1st century BCE, Roman Senator and orator <a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a> commented on the importance of the <a href="/wiki/Tas-Sil%C4%A1" title="Tas-Silġ">Temple of Juno</a>, and on the extravagant behaviour of the Roman governor of Sicily, <a href="/wiki/Verres" title="Verres">Verres</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vm_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vm-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> During the 1st century BCE the island was mentioned by <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diodorus_Siculus" title="Diodorus Siculus">Diodorus Siculus</a>: the latter praised its harbours, the wealth of its inhabitants, its lavishly decorated houses and the quality of its textile products. In the 2nd century, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a> (r. 117–38) upgraded the status of Malta to <i><a href="/wiki/Municipium" title="Municipium">municipium</a></i> or free town: the island local affairs were administered by four <i><a href="/wiki/Duumviri" title="Duumviri">quattuorviri iuri dicundo</a></i> and a municipal senate, while a Roman <a href="/wiki/Procurator_(Roman)" class="mw-redirect" title="Procurator (Roman)">procurator</a>, living in <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">Mdina</a>, represented the <a href="/wiki/Proconsul" title="Proconsul">proconsul</a> of Sicily.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In 58 CE, <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">Paul the Apostle</a> was washed up on the islands together with <a href="/wiki/Luke_the_Evangelist" title="Luke the Evangelist">Luke the Evangelist</a> after their ship was wrecked on the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">Paul the Apostle</a> remained on the islands three months, preaching the Christian faith, which has since thrived on Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 395, when the <a href="/wiki/Division_of_the_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Division of the Roman Empire">Roman Empire was divided for the last time</a> at the death of <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">Theodosius I</a>, Malta, following Sicily, fell under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Migration_Period" title="Migration Period">Migration Period</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Western_Roman_Empire" title="Fall of the Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire declined</a>, Malta came under attack and was conquered or occupied a number of times.<sup id="cite_ref-cassar56–57_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cassar56–57-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> From 454 to 464 the islands was subdued by the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, and after 464 by the <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">Ostrogoths</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> In 533 <a href="/wiki/Belisarius" title="Belisarius">Belisarius</a>, on his way to conquer the <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">Vandal Kingdom</a> in North Africa, reunited the islands under Imperial (<a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Eastern</a>) rule.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Little is known about the Byzantine rule in Malta: the island depended on the <a href="/wiki/Sicily_(theme)" title="Sicily (theme)">theme of Sicily</a> and had Greek Governors and a small Greek garrison.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> While the bulk of population continued to be constituted by the old, Latinized dwellers, during this period its religious allegiance oscillated between the Pope and the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople">Patriarch of Constantinople</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Byzantine rule introduced <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greek</a> families to the Maltese collective.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Malta remained under the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> until 870, when it fell to the <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ei_62-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ei-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arab_period_and_the_Middle_Ages">Arab period and the Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Arab period and the Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Byzantine_wars" title="Arab–Byzantine wars">Arab–Byzantine wars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Sicily" title="Emirate of Sicily">Emirate of Sicily</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahmuna_Tombstone.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Mahmuna_Tombstone.jpeg/220px-Mahmuna_Tombstone.jpeg" width="220" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Mahmuna_Tombstone.jpeg/330px-Mahmuna_Tombstone.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Mahmuna_Tombstone.jpeg/440px-Mahmuna_Tombstone.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="729" data-file-height="761" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahmuna_Tombstone.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Majmuna_Stone" class="mw-redirect" title="Majmuna Stone">Majmuna Stone</a>, a Roman period marble stone, was reused as a 12th-century tombstone believed to have been found in <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Malta became involved in the <a href="/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Byzantine_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab–Byzantine Wars">Arab–Byzantine Wars</a>, and the conquest of Malta is closely linked with <a href="/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Sicily" title="Muslim conquest of Sicily">that of Sicily</a> that began in 827 after admiral <a href="/wiki/Euphemius_(Sicily)" title="Euphemius (Sicily)">Euphemius</a>' betrayal of his fellow Byzantines, requesting that the <a href="/wiki/Aghlabids" title="Aghlabids">Aghlabids</a> invade the island.<sup id="cite_ref-stan_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stan-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
The Muslim chronicler and geographer <a href="/wiki/Kitab_al-Rawd_al-Mitar" title="Kitab al-Rawd al-Mitar">al-Himyari</a> recounts that in 870 CE, following <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Melite_(870)" title="Siege of Melite (870)">a violent struggle</a> against the occupying Byzantines, the Arab invaders, first led by Halaf al-Hadim, and later by Sawada ibn Muhammad,<sup id="cite_ref-Travel_Malta_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Travel_Malta-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> looted and pillaged the island, destroying the most important buildings, and leaving it practically uninhabited until it was recolonised by the Arabs from Sicily in 1048–1049 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-Travel_Malta_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Travel_Malta-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> It is uncertain whether this new settlement took place as a consequence of demographic expansion in Sicily, as a result of a higher standard of living in Sicily (in which case the recolonisation may have taken place a few decades earlier), or as a result of civil war which broke out among the Arab rulers of Sicily in 1038.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
The <a href="/wiki/Arab_Agricultural_Revolution" title="Arab Agricultural Revolution">Arab Agricultural Revolution</a> introduced new irrigation, some fruits and cotton, and the <a href="/wiki/Siculo-Arabic" title="Siculo-Arabic">Siculo-Arabic</a> language was adopted on the island from Sicily; it would eventually evolve into the <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Christians on the island were allowed <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">freedom of religion</a>; they had to pay <a href="/wiki/Jizya" title="Jizya">jizya</a>, a tax for non-Muslims, but were exempt from the tax that Muslims had to pay (<a href="/wiki/Zakat" title="Zakat">zakat</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-gozmalt_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gozmalt-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norman_conquest">Norman conquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Norman conquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roger_I_of_Sicily.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Roger_I_of_Sicily.jpg/170px-Roger_I_of_Sicily.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ea/Roger_I_of_Sicily.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="193" data-file-height="250" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roger_I_of_Sicily.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Roger_I_of_Sicily" title="Roger I of Sicily">Roger I of Sicily</a> returned Malta to Christian rule.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Norman_invasion_of_Malta" title="Norman invasion of Malta">Norman invasion of Malta</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Normans" title="Normans">Normans</a> <a href="/wiki/Norman_invasion_of_Malta" title="Norman invasion of Malta">attacked</a> Malta in 1091, as part of their <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_Sicily" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman conquest of Sicily">conquest of Sicily</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The Norman leader, <a href="/wiki/Roger_I_of_Sicily" title="Roger I of Sicily">Roger I of Sicily</a>, was welcomed by Christian captives.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The notion that Count Roger I reportedly tore off a portion of his checkered red-and-white banner and presented it to the <a href="/wiki/Maltese_people" title="Maltese people">Maltese</a> in gratitude for having fought on his behalf, forming the basis of the modern <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Malta" title="Flag of Malta">flag of Malta</a>, is founded in myth.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_by_Piri_Reis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Malta_by_Piri_Reis.jpg/170px-Malta_by_Piri_Reis.jpg" width="170" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Malta_by_Piri_Reis.jpg/255px-Malta_by_Piri_Reis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Malta_by_Piri_Reis.jpg/340px-Malta_by_Piri_Reis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="546" data-file-height="812" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_by_Piri_Reis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> map of Malta, by <a href="/wiki/Piri_Reis" title="Piri Reis">Piri Reis</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Norman period was productive; Malta became part of the newly formed <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a> which also covered the island of Sicily and the southern half of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">Italian Peninsula</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Catholic Church was reinstated as the state religion with Malta under the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Palermo" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Palermo">See of Palermo</a>, and some <a href="/wiki/Norman_architecture" title="Norman architecture">Norman architecture</a> sprung up around Malta especially in its ancient capital <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">Mdina</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tancred,_King_of_Sicily" title="Tancred, King of Sicily">Tancred, King of Sicily</a>, the last Norman monarch, made Malta a <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fief</a> of the kingdom and installed a <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Malta" title="Count of Malta">count of Malta</a>. As the islands were much desired due to their strategic importance, it was during this time the men of Malta were <a href="/wiki/Militarization" title="Militarization">militarised</a> to fend off capture attempts; early counts were skilled <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">Genoese</a> <a href="/wiki/Privateer" title="Privateer">privateers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The kingdom passed on to the dynasty of <a href="/wiki/Hohenstaufen" title="Hohenstaufen">Hohenstaufen</a> from 1194 until 1266. During this period, when Frederick II of Hohenstaufen began to reorganise his Sicilian kingdom, Western culture and religion began to exert their influence more intensely.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Malta was declared a county and a <a href="/wiki/Marquess" title="Marquess">marquisate</a>, but its trade was totally ruined. For a long time it remained solely a fortified <a href="/wiki/Garrison" title="Garrison">garrison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A mass expulsion of Arabs occurred in 1224 and the entire Christian male population of <a href="/wiki/Celano" title="Celano">Celano</a> in Abruzzo was deported to Malta in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 1249 <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, decreed that all remaining Muslims be expelled from Malta<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> or impelled to convert.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For a brief period the kingdom passed to the <a href="/wiki/Capetian_House_of_Anjou" title="Capetian House of Anjou">Capetian House of Anjou</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> but high taxes made the dynasty unpopular in Malta, due in part to <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Naples" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles I of Naples">Charles of Anjou</a>'s war against the Republic of Genoa, and the island of <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a> was sacked in 1275.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> A large revolt on Sicily known as the <a href="/wiki/Sicilian_Vespers" title="Sicilian Vespers">Sicilian Vespers</a> followed these attacks, a revolt that saw the Peninsula separating into the Kingdom of Naples.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crown_of_Aragon_rule_and_the_Knights_of_Malta">Crown of Aragon rule and the Knights of Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Crown of Aragon rule and the Knights of Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/County_of_Sicily" title="County of Sicily">County of Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_Malta_under_the_Order_of_Saint_John" title="History of Malta under the Order of Saint John">History of Malta under the Order of Saint John</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Malta" title="Great Siege of Malta">Great Siege of Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandiera_del_Regno_di_Sicilia_4.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bandiera_del_Regno_di_Sicilia_4.svg/220px-Bandiera_del_Regno_di_Sicilia_4.svg.png" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bandiera_del_Regno_di_Sicilia_4.svg/330px-Bandiera_del_Regno_di_Sicilia_4.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Bandiera_del_Regno_di_Sicilia_4.svg/440px-Bandiera_del_Regno_di_Sicilia_4.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="897" data-file-height="612" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bandiera_del_Regno_di_Sicilia_4.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Flag of the Aragonese <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a></div></div></div>
<p>Malta was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Barcelona" title="House of Barcelona">House of Barcelona</a>, an Aragonese dynasty from 1282 to 1409,<sup id="cite_ref-culturalheritage.gov.mt_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culturalheritage.gov.mt-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> with the Aragonese aiding the Maltese insurgents in the <a href="/wiki/Sicilian_Vespers" title="Sicilian Vespers">Sicilian Vespers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Malta" title="Battle of Malta">a naval battle in Grand Harbour in 1283</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Relatives of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Aragonese_monarchs" title="List of Aragonese monarchs">kings of Aragon</a> ruled the island until 1409, when it formally passed to the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a>. Early on in the Aragonese ascendancy, the sons of the monarchy received the title, "Count of Malta". During this time much of the local nobility was created. By 1397, however, the bearing of the title "Count of Malta" reverted to a feudal basis, with two families fighting over the distinction, which caused some conflict. This led the <a href="/wiki/Martin_I_of_Sicily" title="Martin I of Sicily">Martin I of Sicily</a> to abolish the title. Dispute over the title returned when the title was reinstated a few years later and the Maltese, led by the local nobility, rose up against Count Gonsalvo Monroy.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Although they opposed the Count, the Maltese voiced their loyalty to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Sicily" title="List of monarchs of Sicily">Sicilian Crown</a>, which so impressed <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_V_of_Aragon" title="Alfonso V of Aragon">Alfonso V of Aragon</a> that he did not punish the people for their rebellion. Instead, he promised never to grant the title to a third party, and incorporated it back into the crown. The city of <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">Mdina</a> was given the title of <i>Città Notabile</i> as a result of this sequence of events.<sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JPDV.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/JPDV.jpg/170px-JPDV.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/JPDV.jpg/255px-JPDV.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/JPDV.jpg/340px-JPDV.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JPDV.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jean_Parisot_de_Valette" title="Jean Parisot de Valette">Jean Parisot de Valette</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Mdina_BW_2011-10-05_12-41-38.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Malta_Mdina_BW_2011-10-05_12-41-38.JPG/170px-Malta_Mdina_BW_2011-10-05_12-41-38.JPG" width="170" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Malta_Mdina_BW_2011-10-05_12-41-38.JPG/255px-Malta_Mdina_BW_2011-10-05_12-41-38.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Malta_Mdina_BW_2011-10-05_12-41-38.JPG/340px-Malta_Mdina_BW_2011-10-05_12-41-38.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3388" data-file-height="2578" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Mdina_BW_2011-10-05_12-41-38.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Cathedral,_Mdina" title="St. Paul&#39;s Cathedral, Mdina">St. Paul's Cathedral, Mdina</a> built in the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> style</div></div></div>
<p>On 23 March 1530,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, gave the islands to the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights Hospitaller</a> under the leadership of Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Philippe_Villiers_de_L%27Isle-Adam" title="Philippe Villiers de L&#39;Isle-Adam">Philippe Villiers de L'Isle-Adam</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Princes_and_Grand_Masters_of_the_Sovereign_Military_Order_of_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Princes and Grand Masters of the Sovereign Military Order of Malta">Grand Master of the Order</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> in perpetual lease for which they had to pay an annual <a href="/wiki/Tribute_of_the_Maltese_Falcon" title="Tribute of the Maltese Falcon">tribute of one single Maltese Falcon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-odonnel_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-odonnel-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-perez_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perez-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-elpais_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elpais-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tc1_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc1-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tc2_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tc2-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-abc_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abc-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> These knights, a military religious order now known as the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights of Malta</a>, had been driven out of <a href="/wiki/Rhodes" title="Rhodes">Rhodes</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> in 1522.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_John_(chartered_1888)" title="Order of Saint John (chartered 1888)">Order of Saint John</a> (also known as the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights Hospitaller</a>, or the <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_Military_Order_of_Malta" title="Sovereign Military Order of Malta">Knights of Malta</a>) were the rulers of Malta and Gozo between 1530 and 1798.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> During this period, the strategic and military importance of the island grew greatly as the small yet efficient fleet of the Order of Saint John launched their attacks from this new base targeting the shipping lanes of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> territories around the Mediterranean Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1551, the population of the island of <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a> (around 5,000 people) were taken as slaves by <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> and brought to the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_Coast" title="Barbary Coast">Barbary Coast</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelangelo_Caravaggio_021.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Michelangelo_Caravaggio_021.jpg/220px-Michelangelo_Caravaggio_021.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Michelangelo_Caravaggio_021.jpg/330px-Michelangelo_Caravaggio_021.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Michelangelo_Caravaggio_021.jpg/440px-Michelangelo_Caravaggio_021.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="2173" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Michelangelo_Caravaggio_021.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/The_Beheading_of_Saint_John_the_Baptist_(Caravaggio)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Beheading of Saint John the Baptist (Caravaggio)">The Beheading of Saint John</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Caravaggio" title="Caravaggio">Caravaggio</a>. Oil on canvas, 361&#160;cm ×&#160;520&#160;cm (142.13&#160;<a href="/wiki/Inch" title="Inch">in</a> ×&#160;204.72&#160;in). Oratory of the <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Co-Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s Co-Cathedral">Co-Cathedral</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The knights, led by Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Jean_Parisot_de_Valette" title="Jean Parisot de Valette">Jean Parisot de Valette</a>, Grand Master of the Order, withstood the <a href="/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Malta" title="Great Siege of Malta">Great Siege of Malta</a> by the Ottomans in 1565.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The knights, with the help of Spanish and Maltese forces, were victorious and repelled the attack. Speaking of the battle <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> said, "Nothing is better known than the siege of Malta."<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> After the siege they decided to increase Malta's <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">fortifications</a>, particularly in the inner-harbour area, where the new city of <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>, named in honour of Valette, was built. They also established <a href="/wiki/Watchtower" title="Watchtower">watchtowers</a> along the coasts&#160;– the <a href="/wiki/Wignacourt_towers" title="Wignacourt towers">Wignacourt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lascaris_towers" title="Lascaris towers">Lascaris</a> and <a href="/wiki/De_Redin_towers" title="De Redin towers">De Redin towers</a>&#160;– named after the Grand Masters who ordered the work. The Knights' presence on the island saw the completion of many architectural and cultural projects, including the embellishment of Città Vittoriosa (modern <a href="/wiki/Birgu" title="Birgu">Birgu</a>), the construction of new cities including Città Rohan (modern <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBebbu%C4%A1" title="Żebbuġ">Żebbuġ</a>) . Zebbug is one of the oldest cities of Malta, it also has one of the largest squares of Malta.
</p><p>Città Hompesch (modern <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBabbar" title="Żabbar">Żabbar</a>) is a village which is also very old. Approximately 11,000 people out of a population of 60,000 died of <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> in 1675.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_period">French period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: French period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/French_occupation_of_Malta" title="French occupation of Malta">French occupation of Malta</a></div>
<p>The Knights' reign ended when <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I of France">Napoleon</a> captured Malta on his way to <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars:_Campaigns_of_1798" class="mw-redirect" title="French Revolutionary Wars: Campaigns of 1798">French Revolutionary Wars</a> in 1798. Over the years preceding Napoleon's capture of the islands, the power of the Knights had declined and the Order had become unpopular. This was around the time when the universal values of freedom and liberty were incarnated by the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>. People from both inside the Order and outside appealed to <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> to oust the Knights. Napoleon Bonaparte did not hesitate. His fleet arrived in 1798, en route to his expedition of Egypt. As a ruse towards the Knights, Napoleon asked for safe harbour to resupply his ships, and then turned his guns against his hosts once safely inside Valletta. Grand Master <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_von_Hompesch_zu_Bolheim" title="Ferdinand von Hompesch zu Bolheim">Hompesch</a> capitulated, and Napoleon entered Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleonbonapartemalta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Napoleonbonapartemalta.jpg/150px-Napoleonbonapartemalta.jpg" width="150" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Napoleonbonapartemalta.jpg/225px-Napoleonbonapartemalta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Napoleonbonapartemalta.jpg/300px-Napoleonbonapartemalta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Napoleonbonapartemalta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bust of Bonaparte at <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Parisio_(Valletta)" title="Palazzo Parisio (Valletta)">Palazzo Parisio</a> in Valletta</div></div></div>
<p>During 12–18 June 1798, Napoleon resided at the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Parisio_(Valletta)" title="Palazzo Parisio (Valletta)">Palazzo Parisio</a> in Valletta.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> He reformed national administration with the creation of a Government Commission, twelve municipalities, a public finance administration, the abolition of all feudal rights and privileges, the <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Abolitionism in France">abolition of slavery</a> and the granting of freedom to all Turkish and Jewish slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-stbenedict_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stbenedict-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> On the judicial level, a family code was framed and twelve judges were nominated. <a href="/wiki/Public_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Public education">Public education</a> was organised along principles laid down by Bonaparte himself, providing for primary and secondary education.<sup id="cite_ref-stbenedict_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stbenedict-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> He then sailed for Egypt leaving a substantial garrison in Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The French forces left behind became unpopular with the Maltese, due particularly to the French forces' hostility towards Catholicism and pillaging of local churches to fund Napoleon's war efforts. French financial and religious policies so angered the Maltese that they rebelled, forcing the French to depart. Great Britain, along with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Kingdom of Naples</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a>, sent ammunition and aid to the Maltese and Britain also sent <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">her navy</a>, which blockaded the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-stbenedict_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stbenedict-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>General <a href="/wiki/Claude-Henri_Belgrand_de_Vaubois" title="Claude-Henri Belgrand de Vaubois">Claude-Henri Belgrand de Vaubois</a> surrendered his French forces in 1800.<sup id="cite_ref-stbenedict_111-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stbenedict-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Maltese leaders presented the island to Sir <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Ball" title="Alexander Ball">Alexander Ball</a>, asking that the island become a British <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a>. The Maltese people created a Declaration of Rights in which they agreed to come "under the protection and sovereignty of the King of the free people, His Majesty the King of the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland". The Declaration also stated that "his Majesty has no right to cede these Islands to any power...if he chooses to withdraw his protection, and abandon his sovereignty, the right of electing another sovereign, or of the governing of these Islands, belongs to us, the inhabitants and aborigines alone, and without control."<sup id="cite_ref-stbenedict_111-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stbenedict-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Empire_and_the_Second_World_War">British Empire and the Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: British Empire and the Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Malta_Protectorate" title="Malta Protectorate">Malta Protectorate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crown_Colony_of_Malta" title="Crown Colony of Malta">Crown Colony of Malta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">Siege of Malta (World War II)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_palazzo_parisio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/British_palazzo_parisio.jpg/150px-British_palazzo_parisio.jpg" width="150" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/British_palazzo_parisio.jpg/225px-British_palazzo_parisio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/British_palazzo_parisio.jpg/300px-British_palazzo_parisio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1532" data-file-height="2052" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_palazzo_parisio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plaque of the <a href="/wiki/Rights_of_man" class="mw-redirect" title="Rights of man">Rights of man</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony_of_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown colony of Malta">British Protectorate</a> (1802) at <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Parisio_(Valletta)" title="Palazzo Parisio (Valletta)">Palazzo Parisio</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BombDamageMalta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BombDamageMalta.jpg/220px-BombDamageMalta.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BombDamageMalta.jpg/330px-BombDamageMalta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/BombDamageMalta.jpg/440px-BombDamageMalta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="606" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BombDamageMalta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The heavily bomb-damaged Kingsway (now Republic Street) in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">Siege of Malta</a>, 1942</div></div></div>
<p>In 1814, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1814)" title="Treaty of Paris (1814)">Treaty of Paris</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-stbenedict_111-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stbenedict-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DIC_11_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DIC_11-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Malta officially became a part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> and was used as a shipping way-station and fleet headquarters. After the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> opened in 1869, Malta's position halfway between the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> and Egypt proved to be its main asset, and it was considered an important stop on the way to India, a central trade route for the British. Because of its position, several culinary and botanical products were introduced in Malta; some examples (derived from the National Book of Trade Customs found in the National Library) include wheat (for bread making) and <a href="/wiki/Bacon" title="Bacon">bacon</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Between 1915 and 1918, during the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, Malta became known as <i>the Nurse of the Mediterranean</i> due to the large number of wounded soldiers who were accommodated in Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In 1919 British troops fired on a rally protesting against new taxes, killing four Maltese men. The event, known as <a href="/wiki/Sette_Giugno" title="Sette Giugno">Sette Giugno</a> (Italian for <i>7 June</i>), is commemorated every year and is one of five National Days.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, Valletta was the location of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/British_Mediterranean_Fleet" class="mw-redirect" title="British Mediterranean Fleet">Mediterranean Fleet</a>'s headquarters. However, despite <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>'s objections,<sup id="cite_ref-BJandCS-p36_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BJandCS-p36-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> the command was moved to <a href="/wiki/Alexandria" title="Alexandria">Alexandria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, in April 1937 out of fear that it was too susceptible to air attacks from Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-BJandCS-p36_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BJandCS-p36-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ElliottP--pxx_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElliottP--pxx-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the Second World War, Malta played an important role for the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a>; being a British colony, situated close to Sicily and the <a href="/wiki/Axis_Powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Axis Powers">Axis</a> shipping lanes, Malta was bombarded by the Italian and German air forces. Malta was used by the British to launch attacks on the Italian navy and had a submarine base. It was also used as a listening post, intercepting German radio messages including <a href="/wiki/Enigma_(machine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Enigma (machine)">Enigma</a> traffic.<sup id="cite_ref-CP-p42-44_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CP-p42-44-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The bravery of the Maltese people during the second <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">Siege of Malta</a> moved <a href="/wiki/George_VI_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="George VI of the United Kingdom">King George VI</a> to award the <a href="/wiki/Award_of_the_George_Cross_to_Malta" title="Award of the George Cross to Malta">George Cross</a> to Malta on a collective basis on 15 April 1942 "to bear witness to a heroism and devotion that will long be famous in history". Some historians argue that the award caused Britain to incur disproportionate losses in defending Malta, as British credibility would have suffered if Malta surrendered, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Singapore" title="Battle of Singapore">as British forces in Singapore had done</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> A depiction of the George Cross now appears in the upper hoist corner of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Malta" title="Flag of Malta">Flag of Malta</a>. The collective award remained unique until April 1999, when the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ulster_Constabulary" title="Royal Ulster Constabulary">Royal Ulster Constabulary</a> became the second&#160;&#8211;&#32;and, to date, the only other&#160;&#8211;&#32;recipient of a collective George Cross.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_Republic">Independence and Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Independence and Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/State_of_Malta" title="State of Malta">State of Malta</a></div>
