<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Denkmal_an_die_Unabh%C3%A4ngigkeit_Maltas_in_Valletta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Denkmal_an_die_Unabh%C3%A4ngigkeit_Maltas_in_Valletta.jpg/220px-Denkmal_an_die_Unabh%C3%A4ngigkeit_Maltas_in_Valletta.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Denkmal_an_die_Unabh%C3%A4ngigkeit_Maltas_in_Valletta.jpg/330px-Denkmal_an_die_Unabh%C3%A4ngigkeit_Maltas_in_Valletta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Denkmal_an_die_Unabh%C3%A4ngigkeit_Maltas_in_Valletta.jpg/440px-Denkmal_an_die_Unabh%C3%A4ngigkeit_Maltas_in_Valletta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Denkmal_an_die_Unabh%C3%A4ngigkeit_Maltas_in_Valletta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Monument to the independence of Malta in <a href="/wiki/Floriana" title="Floriana">Floriana</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Malta joined the European Union in 2004 and signed the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Treaty">Lisbon Treaty</a> in 2007.</div></div></div>
<p>Malta achieved its independence as the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Malta" title="State of Malta">State of Malta</a> on 21 September 1964 (<a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Malta)" title="Independence Day (Malta)">Independence Day</a>) after intense negotiations with the United Kingdom, led by Maltese Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/George_Bor%C4%A1_Olivier" class="mw-redirect" title="George Borġ Olivier">George Borġ Olivier</a>. Under its 1964 constitution, Malta initially retained Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Elizabeth II of the United Kingdom">Elizabeth II</a> as <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Malta" title="Queen of Malta">Queen of Malta</a> and thus <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Governor-general" title="Governor-general">governor-general</a> exercising executive authority on her behalf. In 1971, the <a href="/wiki/Malta_Labour_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Malta Labour Party">Malta Labour Party</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Dom_Mintoff" title="Dom Mintoff">Dom Mintoff</a> won the general elections, resulting in Malta declaring itself a republic on 13 December 1974 (<a href="/wiki/Republic_Day_(Malta)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic Day (Malta)">Republic Day</a>) within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Malta" title="President of Malta">President</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. A defence agreement was signed soon after independence, and after being re-negotiated in 1972, expired on 31 March 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Upon its expiry, the British base closed down and all lands formerly controlled by the British on the island were given up to the Maltese government.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta adopted a policy of <a href="/wiki/Neutral_country" title="Neutral country">neutrality</a> in 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In 1989, Malta was the venue of a <a href="/wiki/Malta_Summit" title="Malta Summit">summit</a> between US President <a href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush" class="mw-redirect" title="George H.W. Bush">George H.W. Bush</a> and Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>, their first face-to-face encounter, which signalled the end of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 16 July 1990, Malta, through its foreign minister, <a href="/wiki/Guido_de_Marco" title="Guido de Marco">Guido de Marco</a>, applied to join the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> After tough negotiations, a referendum was held on 8 March 2003, which resulted in a favourable vote.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> General Elections held on 12 April 2003, gave a clear mandate to the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Fenech_Adami" title="Eddie Fenech Adami">Eddie Fenech Adami</a>, to sign the treaty of accession to the European Union on 16 April 2003 in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> on 1 May 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Following the European Council of 21–22 June 2007, Malta joined the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> on 1 January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(September 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Valletta_BW_2011-10-07_10-41-05.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Malta_Valletta_BW_2011-10-07_10-41-05.JPG/220px-Malta_Valletta_BW_2011-10-07_10-41-05.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Malta_Valletta_BW_2011-10-07_10-41-05.JPG/330px-Malta_Valletta_BW_2011-10-07_10-41-05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Malta_Valletta_BW_2011-10-07_10-41-05.JPG/440px-Malta_Valletta_BW_2011-10-07_10-41-05.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3431" data-file-height="2566" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Valletta_BW_2011-10-07_10-41-05.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Courts_of_Justice_building_(Valletta)" title="Courts of Justice building (Valletta)">Courts of Justice building</a> in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Malta" title="Politics of Malta">Politics of Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Malta" title="Government of Malta">Government of Malta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Malta" title="Law of Malta">Law of Malta</a></div>
<p>Malta is a republic<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> whose <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Public_administration" title="Public administration">public administration</a> are closely modelled on the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a>. Malta had the second-highest <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">voter turnout</a> in the world (and the highest for nations without <a href="/wiki/Mandatory_voting" class="mw-redirect" title="Mandatory voting">mandatory voting</a>), based on election turnout in national <a href="/wiki/Lower_house" title="Lower house">lower house</a> elections from 1960 to 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> Parliament is made up of the President and the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives of Malta">House of Representatives</a> (Maltese: <i>Kamra tad-Deputati</i>), which is elected by direct universal suffrage through <a href="/wiki/Single_transferable_vote" title="Single transferable vote">single transferable vote</a> every five years, unless the House is dissolved earlier by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Malta" title="President of Malta">President</a> either on advice of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Malta" title="Prime Minister of Malta">Prime Minister</a> or through the adoption of a motion of no confidence carried within the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives of Malta">House of Representatives</a> and not overturned within three days. In either of these cases, the President may alternatively choose to invite another Member of Parliament who invariably should command the majority of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives of Malta">House of Representatives</a> to form an alternative government for the remainder of the legislature.
</p><p>The House of Representatives is nominally made up of 65 members of parliament whereby 5 members of parliament are elected from each of the thirteen electoral districts. However, where a party wins an absolute majority of votes, but does not have a majority of seats, that party is given additional seats to ensure a parliamentary majority. The 80th article of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Malta" title="Constitution of Malta">Constitution of Malta</a> provides that the president appoint as prime minister "... the member of the House of Representatives who, in his judgment, is best able to command the support of a majority of the members of that House".<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Malta" title="President of Malta">President of Malta</a> is appointed for a five-year term by a resolution of the House of Representatives carried by a simple majority. The role of the president as head of state is largely ceremonial. The main political parties are the <a href="/wiki/Partit_Nazzjonalista" class="mw-redirect" title="Partit Nazzjonalista">Nationalist Party</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian democratic</a> party, and the <a href="/wiki/Partit_Laburista" class="mw-redirect" title="Partit Laburista">Labour Party</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social democratic</a> party. As of 2018 the Labour Party is at the helm of the government, the Prime Minister being <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Muscat" title="Joseph Muscat">Joseph Muscat</a>. The Nationalist Party, with <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Delia" title="Adrian Delia">Adrian Delia</a> as its leader, is in opposition. The <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Malta)" title="Democratic Party (Malta)">Democratic Party</a> is the only small party which has two seats in parliament; the seats were gained when the Democratic Party contested under the Nationalist Party candidate grouping in the 2017 elections but this arrangement was later terminated in that same year. There are small political parties in Malta which have no parliamentary representation.
</p><p>Until the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, Maltese politics was dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Malta" title="Languages of Malta">language question</a> fought out by <a href="/wiki/Italophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Italophone">Italophone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anglophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglophone">Anglophone</a> parties.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Post-war politics dealt with constitutional questions on the relations with Britain (first with <a href="/wiki/Maltese_integration_into_the_United_Kingdom_referendum,_1956" class="mw-redirect" title="Maltese integration into the United Kingdom referendum, 1956">integration</a> then <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Malta)" title="Independence Day (Malta)">independence</a>) and, eventually, relations with the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Malta#EU_membership" title="History of Malta">European Union</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Local_councils_of_Malta" title="Local councils of Malta">Local councils of Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Malta" title="Districts of Malta">Districts of Malta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Malta" title="Regions of Malta">Regions of Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_administrative_division.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Malta_-_administrative_division.svg/220px-Malta_-_administrative_division.svg.png" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Malta_-_administrative_division.svg/330px-Malta_-_administrative_division.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Malta_-_administrative_division.svg/440px-Malta_-_administrative_division.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_administrative_division.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Local_councils_of_Malta" title="Local councils of Malta">Administrative divisions</a> of Malta</div></div></div>
<p>Malta has had a system of local government since 1993,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> based on the <a href="/wiki/European_Charter_of_Local_Self-Government" title="European Charter of Local Self-Government">European Charter of Local Self-Government</a>. The country is divided into <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Malta" title="Regions of Malta">five regions</a> (one of them being Gozo), with each region having its own Regional Committee, serving as the intermediate level between local government and national government.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> The regions are divided into <a href="/wiki/Local_councils_of_Malta" title="Local councils of Malta">local councils</a>, of which there are currently 68 (54 in Malta and 14 in <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>). Sixteen "hamlets", which form part of larger councils, have their own Administrative Committee. The <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Malta" title="Districts of Malta">six districts</a> (five on Malta and the sixth being Gozo) serve primarily statistical purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each council is made up of a number of councillors (from 5 to 13, depending on and relative to the population they represent). A mayor and a <a href="/wiki/Deputy_mayor" title="Deputy mayor">deputy mayor</a> are elected by and from the councillors. The executive secretary, who is appointed by the council, is the executive, administrative and financial head of the council. Councillors are elected every four years through the <a href="/wiki/Single_transferable_vote" title="Single transferable vote">single transferable vote</a>. People who are eligible to vote in the election of the Maltese <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives of Malta">House of Representatives</a> as well as resident <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">citizens of the EU</a> are eligible to vote. Due to system reforms, no elections were held before 2012. Since then, elections have been held every two years for an alternating half of the councils.
</p><p>Local councils are responsible for the general upkeep and embellishment of the locality (including repairs to non-arterial roads), allocation of local wardens and refuse collection; they also carry out general administrative duties for the central government such as collection of government rents and funds and answer government-related public inquiries. Additionally, a number of individual towns and villages in the Republic of Malta have <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Malta" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Malta">sister cities</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Malta" title="Armed Forces of Malta">Armed Forces of Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_111205-N-FV216-139_The_Armed_Forces_of_Malta_counter_piracy_vessel_protection_detachment_demonstrates_aerial_boarding_procedures_during_Eur.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/US_Navy_111205-N-FV216-139_The_Armed_Forces_of_Malta_counter_piracy_vessel_protection_detachment_demonstrates_aerial_boarding_procedures_during_Eur.jpg/220px-US_Navy_111205-N-FV216-139_The_Armed_Forces_of_Malta_counter_piracy_vessel_protection_detachment_demonstrates_aerial_boarding_procedures_during_Eur.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/US_Navy_111205-N-FV216-139_The_Armed_Forces_of_Malta_counter_piracy_vessel_protection_detachment_demonstrates_aerial_boarding_procedures_during_Eur.jpg/330px-US_Navy_111205-N-FV216-139_The_Armed_Forces_of_Malta_counter_piracy_vessel_protection_detachment_demonstrates_aerial_boarding_procedures_during_Eur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/US_Navy_111205-N-FV216-139_The_Armed_Forces_of_Malta_counter_piracy_vessel_protection_detachment_demonstrates_aerial_boarding_procedures_during_Eur.jpg/440px-US_Navy_111205-N-FV216-139_The_Armed_Forces_of_Malta_counter_piracy_vessel_protection_detachment_demonstrates_aerial_boarding_procedures_during_Eur.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4145" data-file-height="2770" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_111205-N-FV216-139_The_Armed_Forces_of_Malta_counter_piracy_vessel_protection_detachment_demonstrates_aerial_boarding_procedures_during_Eur.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Protector-class_coastal_patrol_boat" title="Protector-class coastal patrol boat"><i>Protector</i>-class patrol boats</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Squadron_of_the_Armed_Forces_of_Malta" title="Maritime Squadron of the Armed Forces of Malta">Maritime Squadron of the AFM</a></div></div></div>
<p>The objectives of the Armed Forces of Malta (AFM) are to maintain a military organisation with the primary aim of defending the islands' integrity according to the defence roles as set by the government in an efficient and cost-effective manner. This is achieved by emphasising the maintenance of Malta's territorial waters and airspace integrity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The AFM also engages in combating terrorism, fighting against illicit drug trafficking, conducting anti-illegal immigrant operations and patrols and anti-illegal fishing operations, operating <a href="/wiki/Search_and_rescue" title="Search and rescue">search and rescue</a> (SAR) services, and physical or electronic security and surveillance of sensitive locations. Malta's search-and-rescue area extends from east of <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> to west of <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a>, covering an area of around 250,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>As a military organisation, the AFM provides backup support to the <a href="/wiki/Malta_Police_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Malta Police Force">Malta Police Force</a> (MPF) and other government departments/agencies in situations as required in an organised, disciplined manner in the event of national emergencies (such as natural disasters) or internal security and bomb disposal.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On another level, the AFM establishes or consolidates <a href="/wiki/Bilateralism" title="Bilateralism">bilateral co-operation</a> with other countries to reach higher operational effectiveness related to AFM roles.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Malta" title="Geography of Malta">Geography of Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:General_map_of_Malta.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/General_map_of_Malta.svg/220px-General_map_of_Malta.svg.png" width="220" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/General_map_of_Malta.svg/330px-General_map_of_Malta.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/General_map_of_Malta.svg/440px-General_map_of_Malta.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="502" data-file-height="433" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:General_map_of_Malta.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Topographic map of Malta</div></div></div>
<p>Malta is an <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> in the central <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> (in its eastern basin), some 80&#160;km (50&#160;mi) south of the Italian island of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Malta_Channel" title="Malta Channel">Malta Channel</a>. Only the three largest islands&#160;– <a href="/wiki/Malta_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Malta Island">Malta</a> (Malta), <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a> (Għawdex) and <a href="/wiki/Comino" title="Comino">Comino</a> (Kemmuna)&#160;– are inhabited. The smaller islands (see below) are uninhabited. The islands of the archipelago lie on the Malta plateau, a shallow shelf formed from the high points of a <a href="/wiki/Land_bridge" title="Land bridge">land bridge</a> between Sicily and North Africa that became isolated as sea levels rose after the last <a href="/wiki/Ice_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice Age">Ice Age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> The archipelago is therefore situated in the zone between the Eurasian and African tectonic plates.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
Malta was considered an island of North Africa for centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Numerous bays along the indented coastline of the islands provide good harbours. The landscape consists of low hills with terraced fields. The highest point in Malta is <a href="/wiki/Ta%27_Dmejrek" title="Ta&#39; Dmejrek">Ta' Dmejrek</a>, at 253&#160;m (830&#160;ft), near <a href="/wiki/Dingli" title="Dingli">Dingli</a>. Although there are some small rivers at times of high rainfall, there are no permanent rivers or lakes on Malta. However, some watercourses have fresh water running all year round at <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%A7rija" title="Baħrija">Baħrija</a> near <a href="/wiki/Ras_ir-Ra%C4%A7eb" title="Ras ir-Raħeb">Ras ir-Raħeb</a>, at l-Imtaħleb and San Martin, and at Lunzjata Valley in Gozo.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Malta belongs to the Liguro-Tyrrhenian province of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean Region">Mediterranean Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, the territory of Malta belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of "Mediterranean Forests, Woodlands and Scrub".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Nature_Reserve_from_St._Agatha%27s_Tower.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/View_of_Nature_Reserve_from_St._Agatha%27s_Tower.JPG/220px-View_of_Nature_Reserve_from_St._Agatha%27s_Tower.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/View_of_Nature_Reserve_from_St._Agatha%27s_Tower.JPG/330px-View_of_Nature_Reserve_from_St._Agatha%27s_Tower.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/View_of_Nature_Reserve_from_St._Agatha%27s_Tower.JPG/440px-View_of_Nature_Reserve_from_St._Agatha%27s_Tower.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Nature_Reserve_from_St._Agatha%27s_Tower.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maltese landscape, Għadira</div></div></div>
<p>The minor islands that form part of the archipelago are uninhabited and include:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em;">
<ul><li>Barbaġanni Rock (<a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cominotto" title="Cominotto">Cominotto</a>, (<i>Kemmunett</i>)</li>
<li>Dellimara Island (<a href="/wiki/Marsaxlokk" title="Marsaxlokk">Marsaxlokk</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Filfla" title="Filfla">Filfla</a> (<a href="/wiki/%C5%BBurrieq" title="Żurrieq">Żurrieq</a>)/(<a href="/wiki/Si%C4%A1%C4%A1iewi" title="Siġġiewi">Siġġiewi</a>)</li>
<li>Fessej Rock</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fungus_Rock" title="Fungus Rock">Fungus Rock</a>, (<i>Il-Ġebla tal-Ġeneral</i>) (<a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>)</li>
<li>Għallis Rock (<a href="/wiki/Naxxar" title="Naxxar">Naxxar</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C4%A6alfa_Rock" title="Ħalfa Rock">Ħalfa Rock</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>)</li>
<li>Large Blue Lagoon Rocks (<a href="/wiki/Comino" title="Comino">Comino</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Islands_of_St._Paul" class="mw-redirect" title="Islands of St. Paul">Islands of St. Paul</a>/Selmunett Island (<a href="/wiki/Mellie%C4%A7a" title="Mellieħa">Mellieħa</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manoel_Island" title="Manoel Island">Manoel Island</a>, which connects to the town of <a href="/wiki/G%C5%BCira" title="Gżira">Gżira</a>, on the mainland, via a bridge</li>
<li>Mistra Rocks (<a href="/wiki/San_Pawl_il-Ba%C4%A7ar" class="mw-redirect" title="San Pawl il-Baħar">San Pawl il-Baħar</a>)</li>
<li>Taċ-Ċawl Rock (<a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>)</li>
<li>Qawra Point/Ta' Fraben Island (<a href="/wiki/San_Pawl_il-Ba%C4%A7ar" class="mw-redirect" title="San Pawl il-Baħar">San Pawl il-Baħar</a>)</li>
<li>Small Blue Lagoon Rocks (<a href="/wiki/Comino" title="Comino">Comino</a>)</li>
<li>Sala Rock (<a href="/wiki/%C5%BBabbar" title="Żabbar">Żabbar</a>)</li>
<li>Xrobb l-Għaġin Rock (<a href="/wiki/Marsaxlokk" title="Marsaxlokk">Marsaxlokk</a>)</li>
<li>Ta' taħt il-Mazz Rock</li></ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Malta" title="Climate of Malta">Climate of Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Lagoon_and_Cominotto.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Blue_Lagoon_and_Cominotto.JPG/220px-Blue_Lagoon_and_Cominotto.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Blue_Lagoon_and_Cominotto.JPG/330px-Blue_Lagoon_and_Cominotto.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Blue_Lagoon_and_Cominotto.JPG/440px-Blue_Lagoon_and_Cominotto.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blue_Lagoon_and_Cominotto.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Blue Lagoon Bay between <a href="/wiki/Comino" title="Comino">Comino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cominotto" title="Cominotto">Cominotto</a> island</div></div></div>
<p>Malta has a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Csa</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-cia_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> with mild winters and hot summers, hotter in the inland areas. Rain occurs mainly in autumn and winter, with summer being generally dry.
</p><p>The average yearly temperature is around 23&#160;°C (73&#160;°F) during the day and 15.5&#160;°C (59.9&#160;°F) at night. In the coldest month&#160;– January&#160;– the typical maximum temperature ranges from 12 to 18&#160;°C (54 to 64&#160;°F) during the day and minimum 6 to 12&#160;°C (43 to 54&#160;°F) at night. In the warmest month&#160;– August&#160;– the typical maximum temperature ranges from 28 to 34&#160;°C (82 to 93&#160;°F) during the day and minimum 20 to 24&#160;°C (68 to 75&#160;°F) at night. Amongst all capitals in the continent of Europe, Valletta&#160;– the capital of Malta has the warmest winters, with average temperatures of around 15 to 16&#160;°C (59 to 61&#160;°F) during the day and 9 to 10&#160;°C (48 to 50&#160;°F) at night in the period January–February. In March and December average temperatures are around 17&#160;°C (63&#160;°F) during the day and 11&#160;°C (52&#160;°F) at night.<sup id="cite_ref-Met_Office_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Met_Office-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Large fluctuations in temperature are rare. Snow is very rare on the island, although various snowfalls have been recorded in the last century, the last one reported in various locations across Malta in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The average annual sea temperature is 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F), from 15–16&#160;°C (59–61&#160;°F) in February to 26&#160;°C (79&#160;°F) in August. In the 6 months&#160;– from June to November&#160;– the average sea temperature exceeds 20&#160;°C (68&#160;°F).<sup id="cite_ref-weather2travel_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather2travel-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-maltaweather_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maltaweather-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The annual average <a href="/wiki/Relative_humidity" title="Relative humidity">relative humidity</a> is high, averaging 75%, ranging from 65% in July (morning: 78% evening: 53%) to 80% in December (morning: 83% evening: 73%).<sup id="cite_ref-weatherbase.com_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weatherbase.com-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sunshine_duration" title="Sunshine duration">Sunshine duration</a> hours total around 3,000 per year, from an average 5.2 hours of sunshine duration per day in December to an average above 12 hours in July.<sup id="cite_ref-maltaweather_149-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-maltaweather-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-noaa_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noaa-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> This is about double that of cities in the northern half of Europe, for comparison: London&#160;– 1,461;<sup id="cite_ref-London_climate_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_climate-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> however, in winter it has up to four times more sunshine; for comparison: in December, London has 37 hours of sunshine<sup id="cite_ref-London_climate_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-London_climate-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> whereas Malta has above 160.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Urbanisation">Urbanisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Urbanisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valletta,_Malta.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Valletta%2C_Malta.JPG/330px-Valletta%2C_Malta.JPG" width="330" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Valletta%2C_Malta.JPG/495px-Valletta%2C_Malta.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a6/Valletta%2C_Malta.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="437" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valletta,_Malta.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main urban area of Malta. <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a> is the central peninsula.</div></div></div>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, Malta is composed of two <a href="/wiki/Larger_urban_zones" class="mw-redirect" title="Larger urban zones">larger urban zones</a> nominally referred to as "Valletta" (the main island of Malta) and "Gozo". According to <a href="/wiki/Demographia" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographia">Demographia</a>, state<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (July 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> is identified as an urban area.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/European_Spatial_Planning_Observation_Network" class="mw-redirect" title="European Spatial Planning Observation Network">European Spatial Planning Observation Network</a>, Malta is identified as functional urban area (FUA).<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> According to United Nations, about 95 per cent of the area of Malta is urban and the number grows every year.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Also, according to the results of ESPON and EU Commission studies, "<i>the whole territory of Malta constitutes a single urban region</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Occasionally in the media and official publications Malta is referred to as a <a href="/wiki/City-state" title="City-state">city-state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Also, the Maltese coat-of-arms bears a <a href="/wiki/Mural_crown" title="Mural crown">mural crown</a> described as "representing the fortifications of Malta and denoting a City State".<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> Malta, with area of 316&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (122&#160;sq&#160;mi) and population of 0.4&#160;million, is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">most densely populated</a> countries worldwide.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Malta" title="Economy of Malta">Economy of Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AIDAcara_Valetta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/AIDAcara_Valetta.jpg/220px-AIDAcara_Valetta.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/AIDAcara_Valetta.jpg/330px-AIDAcara_Valetta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/AIDAcara_Valetta.jpg/440px-AIDAcara_Valetta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AIDAcara_Valetta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Valletta's maritime industrial zone</div></div></div>
<p>Malta is classified as an <a href="/wiki/Advanced_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced economy">advanced economy</a> together with 32 other countries according to the International Monetary Fund (IMF).<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Until 1800 Malta depended on cotton, tobacco and its shipyards for exports. Once under British control, they came to depend on <a href="/wiki/Malta_Dockyard" title="Malta Dockyard">Malta Dockyard</a> for support of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>, especially during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> of 1854. The military base benefited craftsmen and all those who served the military.
</p><p>In 1869, the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> gave Malta's economy a great boost, as there was a massive increase in the shipping which entered the port. Ships stopping at Malta's docks for refuelling helped the <a href="/wiki/Entrep%C3%B4t" title="Entrepôt">Entrepôt</a> trade, which brought additional benefits to the island.
</p><p>However, towards the end of the 19th century the economy began declining, and by the 1940s Malta's economy was in serious crisis. One factor was the longer range of newer merchant ships that required less frequent refuelling stops.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mediterraneo_dolphin_show_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mediterraneo_dolphin_show_1.JPG/220px-Mediterraneo_dolphin_show_1.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mediterraneo_dolphin_show_1.JPG/330px-Mediterraneo_dolphin_show_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mediterraneo_dolphin_show_1.JPG/440px-Mediterraneo_dolphin_show_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mediterraneo_dolphin_show_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The dolphin show at Mediterraneo Marine Park. Tourism generates a significant part of the GDP of Malta.</div></div></div>
<p>Currently, Malta's major resources are <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, a favourable geographic location and a productive labour force. Malta produces only about 20 per cent of its food needs, has limited freshwater supplies because of the drought in the summer and has no domestic energy sources, aside from the potential for solar energy from its plentiful sunlight. The economy is dependent on foreign trade (serving as a freight trans-shipment point), manufacturing (especially electronics and textiles) and tourism.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Films_shot_in_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="Films shot in Malta">Film production</a> is a growing contributor to the Maltese economy.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The first film was shot in Malta in 1925 (<i>Sons of the Sea</i>);<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> over 100 feature films have been entirely or partially filmed in the country since then. Malta has served as a "double" for a wide variety of locations and historic periods including Ancient Greece, Ancient and Modern Rome, Iraq, the Middle East and many more.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The Maltese government introduced financial incentives for filmmakers in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> The current financial incentives to foreign productions as of 2015 stand at 25 per cent with an additional 2 per cent if Malta stands in as Malta; meaning a production can get up to 27 per cent back on their eligible spending incurred in Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurozone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/220px-Eurozone.svg.png" width="220" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/330px-Eurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/440px-Eurozone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurozone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Malta is part of a monetary union, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a> (dark blue)</div></div></div>
<p>The government is investing heavily in education, including college.
</p><p>In preparation for Malta's membership in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, which it joined on 1 May 2004, it <a href="/wiki/Privatization" title="Privatization">privatised</a> some state-controlled firms and liberalised markets. For example, the government announced on 8 January 2007 that it was selling its 40 per cent stake in <a href="/wiki/MaltaPost" title="MaltaPost">MaltaPost</a>, to complete a privatisation process which has been ongoing for the past five years. In 2010, Malta managed to privatise telecommunications, postal services, shipyards and shipbuilding.
</p><p>Malta has a financial regulator, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta_Financial_Services_Authority&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Malta Financial Services Authority (page does not exist)">Malta Financial Services Authority</a> (MFSA), with a strong business development mindset, and the country has been successful in attracting gaming businesses, aircraft and ship registration, credit-card issuing banking licences and also fund administration. Service providers to these industries, including fiduciary and trustee business, are a core part of the growth strategy of the island. Malta has made strong headway in implementing EU Financial Services Directives including UCITs IV and soon AIFMD. As a base for alternative asset managers who must comply with new directives, Malta has attracted a number of key players including IDS, Iconic Funds, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apex_Fund_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Apex Fund Services (page does not exist)">Apex Fund Services</a> and TMF/Customs House.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> are currently discussing the commercial exploitation of the continental shelf between their countries, particularly for petroleum exploration. These discussions are also undergoing between Malta and <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> for similar arrangements.
</p><p>Malta does not have a property tax. Its property market, especially around the harbour area, has been in constant boom, with the prices of apartments in some towns like St Julian's, Sliema and Gzira skyrocketing.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> data, Maltese GDP per capita stood at <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_European_Union#Richest_and_poorest_NUTS_regions_(GDP_PPP_2010)" title="Economy of the European Union">88 per cent of the EU average</a> in 2015 with €21,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Eurostat_2012_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eurostat_2012-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Banking_and_finance">Banking and finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Banking and finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_St._Julian%27s_(Triq_it-Torri_(Sliema))_03_ies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Malta_-_St._Julian%27s_%28Triq_it-Torri_%28Sliema%29%29_03_ies.jpg/220px-Malta_-_St._Julian%27s_%28Triq_it-Torri_%28Sliema%29%29_03_ies.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Malta_-_St._Julian%27s_%28Triq_it-Torri_%28Sliema%29%29_03_ies.jpg/330px-Malta_-_St._Julian%27s_%28Triq_it-Torri_%28Sliema%29%29_03_ies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Malta_-_St._Julian%27s_%28Triq_it-Torri_%28Sliema%29%29_03_ies.jpg/440px-Malta_-_St._Julian%27s_%28Triq_it-Torri_%28Sliema%29%29_03_ies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_St._Julian%27s_(Triq_it-Torri_(Sliema))_03_ies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Portomaso_Business_Tower" title="Portomaso Business Tower">Portomaso Business Tower</a>, the tallest building in Malta</div></div></div>
<p>The two largest commercial banks are <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Valletta" title="Bank of Valletta">Bank of Valletta</a> and <a href="/wiki/HSBC_Bank_Malta" title="HSBC Bank Malta">HSBC Bank Malta</a>, both of which can trace their origins back to the 19th century.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Malta" title="Central Bank of Malta">Central Bank of Malta</a> (Bank Ċentrali ta' Malta) has two key areas of responsibility: the formulation and implementation of monetary policy and the promotion of a sound and efficient financial system. It was established by the Central Bank of Malta Act on 17 April 1968. The Maltese government entered <a href="/wiki/ERM_II" class="mw-redirect" title="ERM II">ERM II</a> on 4 May 2005, and adopted the euro as the country's currency on 1 January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>FinanceMalta is the quasi-governmental organisation tasked with marketing and educating business leaders in coming to Malta and runs seminars and events around the world highlighting the emerging strength of Malta as a jurisdiction for banking and finance and insurance.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Malta" title="Transport in Malta">Transport in Malta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta_bus" class="mw-redirect" title="Malta bus">Malta bus</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Malta_2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Map_of_Malta_2.png/220px-Map_of_Malta_2.png" width="220" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Map_of_Malta_2.png/330px-Map_of_Malta_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Map_of_Malta_2.png/440px-Map_of_Malta_2.png 2x" data-file-width="987" data-file-height="1114" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Malta_2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Principal highways</div></div></div>
<p>Traffic in Malta <a href="/wiki/Driving_on_the_left_or_right" class="mw-redirect" title="Driving on the left or right">drives on the left</a>. Car ownership in Malta is exceedingly high, considering the very small size of the islands; it is the fourth-highest in the European Union. The number of registered cars in 1990 amounted to 182,254, giving an automobile density of 577/km<sup>2</sup> (1,494/sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta has 2,254 kilometres (1,401 miles) of road, 1,972&#160;km (1,225&#160;mi) (87.5 per cent) of which are paved and 282&#160;km (175&#160;mi) were unpaved (as of December 2003).<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
The main roads of Malta from the southernmost point to the northernmost point are these: Triq Birżebbuġa in <a href="/wiki/Bir%C5%BCebbu%C4%A1a" title="Birżebbuġa">Birżebbuġa</a>, <a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7ar_Dalam" title="Għar Dalam">Għar Dalam</a> Road and <a href="/wiki/Tal-Barrani" title="Tal-Barrani">Tal-Barrani</a> Road in <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBejtun" title="Żejtun">Żejtun</a>, Santa Luċija Avenue in <a href="/wiki/Paola,_Malta" title="Paola, Malta">Paola</a>, Aldo Moro Street (Trunk Road), 13 December Street and <a href="/wiki/%C4%A6amrun" title="Ħamrun">Ħamrun</a>-Marsa Bypass in <a href="/wiki/Marsa,_Malta" title="Marsa, Malta">Marsa</a>, Regional Road in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Venera" title="Santa Venera">Santa Venera</a>/<a href="/wiki/Msida" title="Msida">Msida</a>/<a href="/wiki/G%C5%BCira" title="Gżira">Gżira</a>/<a href="/wiki/San_%C4%A0wann" title="San Ġwann">San Ġwann</a>, St Andrew's Road in <a href="/wiki/Swieqi" title="Swieqi">Swieqi</a>/<a href="/wiki/Pembroke,_Malta" title="Pembroke, Malta">Pembroke, Malta</a>, Coast Road in <a href="/wiki/Ba%C4%A7ar_i%C4%8B-%C4%8Aag%C4%A7aq" title="Baħar iċ-Ċagħaq">Baħar iċ-Ċagħaq</a>, Salina Road, Kennedy Drive, St. Paul's Bypass and <a href="/wiki/Xemxija" title="Xemxija">Xemxija</a> Hill in <a href="/wiki/San_Pawl_il-Ba%C4%A7ar" class="mw-redirect" title="San Pawl il-Baħar">San Pawl il-Baħar</a>, Mistra Hill, Wettinger Street (Mellieħa Bypass) and Marfa Road in <a href="/wiki/Mellie%C4%A7a" title="Mellieħa">Mellieħa</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Busse_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Malta_Busse_2016.jpg/220px-Malta_Busse_2016.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Malta_Busse_2016.jpg/330px-Malta_Busse_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Malta_Busse_2016.jpg/440px-Malta_Busse_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Busse_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maltese <i>Otokar</i> buses</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Malta_bus" class="mw-redirect" title="Malta bus">Buses</a> (<i>xarabank</i> or <i>karozza tal-linja</i>) are the primary method of public transport. Established in 1905, they operated in the Maltese islands up to 2011 and became popular tourist attractions in their own right.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> To this day they are depicted on many Maltese advertisements to promote tourism as well as on gifts and merchandise for tourists.
</p><p>The bus service underwent an extensive reform in July 2011. The management structure changed from having self-employed drivers driving their own vehicles to a service being offered by a single company through a public tender (in Gozo, being considered as a small network, the service was given through direct order).<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> The public tender was won by Arriva Malta, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Arriva" title="Arriva">Arriva</a> group, which introduced a fleet of brand new buses, built by <a href="/wiki/King_Long" title="King Long">King Long</a> especially for service by Arriva Malta and including a smaller fleet of <a href="/wiki/Articulated_bus" title="Articulated bus">articulated buses</a> brought in from <a href="/wiki/Arriva_London" title="Arriva London">Arriva London</a>. It also operated two smaller buses for an intra-<a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a> route only and 61 nine-metre buses, which were used to ease congestion on high density routes. Overall Arriva Malta operated 264 buses. On 1 January 2014 Arriva ceased operations in Malta due to financial difficulties, having been nationalised as <i>Malta Public Transport</i> by the Maltese government, with a new bus operator planned to take over their operations in the near future.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The government chose Autobuses Urbanos de León as its preferred bus operator for the country in October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The company took over the bus service on 8 January 2015, while retaining the name <i>Malta Public Transport</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> It introduced the pre-pay 'tallinja card'. With lower fares than the walk-on rate, it can be topped up online. The card was initially not well received, as reported by several local news sites.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> During the first week of August 2015, another 40 buses of the Turkish make <i><a href="/wiki/Otokar" title="Otokar">Otokar</a></i> arrived and were put into service.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1883 to 1931 Malta had a railway line that connected <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a> to the army barracks at <a href="/wiki/Mtarfa" title="Mtarfa">Mtarfa</a> via <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">Mdina</a> and a number of towns and villages. The railway fell into disuse and eventually closed altogether, following the introduction of electric trams and buses.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> At the height of the bombing of Malta during the Second World War, <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Mussolini</a> announced that his forces had destroyed the railway system, but by the time war broke out, the railway had been mothballed for more than nine years.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valletta-Harbour.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Valletta-Harbour.jpg/220px-Valletta-Harbour.jpg" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Valletta-Harbour.jpg/330px-Valletta-Harbour.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Valletta-Harbour.jpg/440px-Valletta-Harbour.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="527" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valletta-Harbour.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Grand_Harbour" title="Grand Harbour">Grand Harbour</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Freeport_from_Pretty_Bay_at_Birzebbuga.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Malta_Freeport_from_Pretty_Bay_at_Birzebbuga.jpg/220px-Malta_Freeport_from_Pretty_Bay_at_Birzebbuga.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Malta_Freeport_from_Pretty_Bay_at_Birzebbuga.jpg/330px-Malta_Freeport_from_Pretty_Bay_at_Birzebbuga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Malta_Freeport_from_Pretty_Bay_at_Birzebbuga.jpg/440px-Malta_Freeport_from_Pretty_Bay_at_Birzebbuga.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Freeport_from_Pretty_Bay_at_Birzebbuga.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Malta_Freeport" title="Malta Freeport">Malta Freeport</a>, one of the largest European ports</div></div></div>
<p>Malta has three large natural harbours on its main island:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Harbour" title="Grand Harbour">Grand Harbour</a> (or Port il-Kbir), located at the eastern side of the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>, has been a harbour since <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> times. It has several extensive <a href="/wiki/Dock_(maritime)" title="Dock (maritime)">docks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wharf" title="Wharf">wharves</a>, as well as a cruise liner terminal. A terminal at the Grand Harbour serves <a href="/wiki/Ferries" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferries">ferries</a> that connect Malta to <a href="/wiki/Pozzallo" title="Pozzallo">Pozzallo</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Catania" title="Catania">Catania</a> in Sicily.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marsamxett_Harbour" title="Marsamxett Harbour">Marsamxett Harbour</a>, located on the western side of Valletta, accommodates a number of yacht marinas.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marsaxlokk_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Marsaxlokk Harbour">Marsaxlokk Harbour</a> (Malta Freeport), at <a href="/wiki/Bir%C5%BCebbu%C4%A1a" title="Birżebbuġa">Birżebbuġa</a> on the south-eastern side of Malta, is the islands' main cargo terminal. Malta Freeport is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_world%27s_busiest_container_ports" class="mw-redirect" title="List of world&#39;s busiest container ports">11th busiest container ports in continent of Europe and 46th in the World</a> with a trade volume of 2.3&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Twenty-foot_equivalent_unit" title="Twenty-foot equivalent unit">TEU's</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>There are also two-man-made harbours that serve a passenger and car ferry service that connects <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Airkewwa" title="Ċirkewwa">Ċirkewwa</a> Harbour on Malta and <a href="/wiki/M%C4%A1arr_(Gozo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mġarr (Gozo)">Mġarr Harbour</a> on <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>. The ferry makes numerous runs each day.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_International_Airport2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Malta_International_Airport2.jpg/220px-Malta_International_Airport2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Malta_International_Airport2.jpg/330px-Malta_International_Airport2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Malta_International_Airport2.jpg/440px-Malta_International_Airport2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_International_Airport2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Malta_International_Airport" title="Malta International Airport">Malta International Airport</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Malta_International_Airport" title="Malta International Airport">Malta International Airport</a> (Ajruport Internazzjonali ta' Malta) is the only airport serving the Maltese islands. It is built on the land formerly occupied by the <a href="/wiki/RAF_Luqa" title="RAF Luqa">RAF Luqa</a> air base. A heliport is also located there, but the scheduled service to Gozo ceased in 2006. The heliport in Gozo is at <a href="/wiki/Xewkija" title="Xewkija">Xewkija</a>. Since June 2007, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Harbour_Air_Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Harbour Air Malta (page does not exist)">Harbour Air Malta</a> has operated a thrice-daily floatplane service between the sea terminal in Grand Harbour and Mgarr Harbour in Gozo.
</p><p>Two further airfields at <a href="/wiki/Ta%27_Qali" title="Ta&#39; Qali">Ta' Qali</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C4%A6al_Far" title="Ħal Far">Ħal Far</a> operated during the Second World War and into the 1960s but are now closed. Today, <a href="/wiki/Ta%27_Qali" title="Ta&#39; Qali">Ta' Qali</a> houses a national park, <a href="/wiki/Ta%27_Qali_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta&#39; Qali Stadium">stadium</a>, the Crafts Village visitor attraction and the <a href="/wiki/Malta_Aviation_Museum" title="Malta Aviation Museum">Malta Aviation Museum</a>. This museum preserves several aircraft, including <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Hurricane" title="Hawker Hurricane">Hurricane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spitfire" class="mw-redirect" title="Spitfire">Spitfire</a> fighters that defended the island in the Second World War.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:9H-AEP_A320_Air_Malta_(14806272801).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/9H-AEP_A320_Air_Malta_%2814806272801%29.jpg/220px-9H-AEP_A320_Air_Malta_%2814806272801%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/9H-AEP_A320_Air_Malta_%2814806272801%29.jpg/330px-9H-AEP_A320_Air_Malta_%2814806272801%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/9H-AEP_A320_Air_Malta_%2814806272801%29.jpg/440px-9H-AEP_A320_Air_Malta_%2814806272801%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:9H-AEP_A320_Air_Malta_(14806272801).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Air Malta <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The national airline is <a href="/wiki/Air_Malta" title="Air Malta">Air Malta</a>, which is based at Malta International Airport and operates services to 36 destinations in Europe and North Africa. The owners of Air Malta are the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Malta" title="Government of Malta">Government of Malta</a> (98 per cent) and private investors (2 percent). Air Malta employs 1,547 staff. It has a 25 per cent shareholding in <a href="/wiki/Medavia" title="Medavia">Medavia</a>.
</p><p>Air Malta has concluded over 191 interline ticketing agreements with other IATA airlines. It also has a codeshare agreement with <a href="/wiki/Qantas" title="Qantas">Qantas</a> covering three routes. In September 2007, Air Malta made two agreements with Abu Dhabi-based Etihad Airways by which Air Malta wet-leased two Airbus aircraft to <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a> for the winter period starting 1 September 2007, and provided operational support on another Airbus A320 aircraft which it leased to Etihad Airways.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The mobile penetration rate in Malta exceeded 100% by the end of 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> Malta uses the <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a>900, UMTS(3G) and LTE(4G) mobile phone systems, which are compatible with the rest of the European countries, Australia and New Zealand.
</p><p>Telephone and cellular subscribers' numbers have eight digits. There are no <a href="/wiki/Area_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Area code">area codes</a> in Malta, but after inception, the original first two numbers, and currently the 3rd and 4th digit, were assigned according to the locality. <a href="/wiki/Fixed_line" class="mw-redirect" title="Fixed line">Fixed line</a> telephone numbers have the prefix 21 and 27, although businesses may have numbers starting 22 or 23. An example would be 2*80**** if from <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBabbar" title="Żabbar">Żabbar</a>, and 2*23**** if from <a href="/wiki/Marsa,_Malta" title="Marsa, Malta">Marsa</a>. Gozitan landline numbers generally are assigned 2*56****. Mobile telephone numbers have the prefix 77, 79, 98 or 99. When calling Malta from abroad, one must first dial the international access code, then the country code +356 and the subscriber's number.
</p><p>The number of pay TV subscribers fell as customers switched to <a href="/wiki/IPTV" title="IPTV">Internet Protocol television</a> (IPTV): the number of IPTV subscribers doubled in the six months to June 2012.
</p><p>In late 2012, <a href="/wiki/GO_(Malta)" title="GO (Malta)">GO</a> began expanding its fibre-to-the-home (FTTH) network and capabilities, offering speeds of up to 200Mbit/s for its 'rapido' service.
</p><p>In early 2012, the government called for a national FttH network to be built, with a minimum broadband service being upgraded from 4Mbit/s to 100Mbit/s.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Currency">Currency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Currency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Maltese_euro_coins" title="Maltese euro coins">Maltese euro coins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Euro_gold_and_silver_commemorative_coins_(Malta)" title="Euro gold and silver commemorative coins (Malta)">Euro gold and silver commemorative coins (Malta)</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Maltese_euro_coins" title="Maltese euro coins">Maltese euro coins</a> feature the <a href="/wiki/Maltese_cross" title="Maltese cross">Maltese cross</a> on €2 and €1 coins, the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Malta" title="Coat of arms of Malta">coat of arms of Malta</a> on the €0.50, €0.20 and €0.10 coins, and the <a href="/wiki/Mnajdra" title="Mnajdra">Mnajdra</a> Temples on the €0.05, €0.02 and €0.01 coins.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta has produced collectors' coins with face value ranging from 10 to 50 euro. These coins continue an existing national practice of minting of silver and gold commemorative coins. Unlike normal issues, these coins are not accepted in all the eurozone. For instance, a €10 Maltese commemorative coin cannot be used in any other country.
</p><p>From 1972 until introduction of the Euro in 2008, the currency was the <a href="/wiki/Maltese_lira" title="Maltese lira">Maltese lira</a>, which had replaced the Maltese pound. The pound replaced the <a href="/wiki/Maltese_scudo" title="Maltese scudo">Maltese scudo</a> in 1825.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mellieha_Bay_beach_Malta_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Mellieha_Bay_beach_Malta_1.jpg/220px-Mellieha_Bay_beach_Malta_1.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Mellieha_Bay_beach_Malta_1.jpg/330px-Mellieha_Bay_beach_Malta_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Mellieha_Bay_beach_Malta_1.jpg/440px-Mellieha_Bay_beach_Malta_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mellieha_Bay_beach_Malta_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mellieħa Bay beach</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Malta" title="Tourism in Malta">Tourism in Malta</a></div>
<p>Malta is a popular tourist destination, with 1.6&#160;million tourists per year.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Three times more tourists visit than there are residents. Tourism infrastructure has increased dramatically over the years and a number of hotels are present on the island, although overdevelopment and the destruction of traditional housing is of growing concern. An increasing number of Maltese now travel abroad on holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In recent years, Malta has advertised itself as a <a href="/wiki/Medical_tourism" title="Medical tourism">medical tourism</a> destination,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> and a number of <a href="/wiki/Health_tourism_provider" class="mw-redirect" title="Health tourism provider">health tourism providers</a> are developing the industry. However, no Maltese hospital has undergone independent <a href="/wiki/International_healthcare_accreditation" title="International healthcare accreditation">international healthcare accreditation</a>. Malta is popular with British medical tourists,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> pointing Maltese hospitals towards seeking UK-sourced accreditation, such as with the <a href="/wiki/Trent_Accreditation_Scheme" title="Trent Accreditation Scheme">Trent Accreditation Scheme</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Science and technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Malta signed a co-operation agreement with the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> (ESA) for more-intensive co-operation in ESA projects.<sup id="cite_ref-Malta_signs_Cooperation_Agreement_with_ESA_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malta_signs_Cooperation_Agreement_with_ESA-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>
The Malta Council for Science and Technology (MCST) is the civil body responsible for the development of science and technology on an educational and social level. Most science students in Malta graduate from the University of Malta and are represented by S-Cubed (Science Student's Society), UESA (University Engineering Students Association) and ICTSA (University of Malta ICT Students' Association).<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Malta" title="Demographics of Malta">Demographics of Malta</a></div>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><tbody><tr><th class="navbox-title" colspan="3"
