style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+10.3%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Source:<sup id="cite_ref-census_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Malta conducts a census of population and housing every ten years. The census held in November 2005 counted an estimated 96 per cent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> A preliminary report was issued in April 2006 and the results were weighted to estimate for 100 per cent of the population.
</p><p>Native <a href="/wiki/Maltese_people" title="Maltese people">Maltese people</a> make up the majority of the island. However, there are minorities, the largest of which are <a href="/wiki/British_people" title="British people">Britons</a>, many of whom are retirees.
The population of Malta as of  July&#160;2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> was estimated at 408,000.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> As of  2005<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 17 per cent were aged 14 and under, 68 per cent were within the 15–64 age bracket whilst the remaining 13 per cent were 65 years and over. Malta's population density of 1,282 per square km (3,322/sq&#160;mi) is by far the highest in the EU and one of the highest in the world. By comparison, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by population density">average population density</a> for the "World (land only, excluding <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>)" was 54&#160;pop./km² as of July 2014.
</p><p>The only census year showing a fall in population was that of 1967, with a 1.7 per cent total decrease, attributable to a substantial number of Maltese residents who emigrated.<sup id="cite_ref-Census2005_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census2005-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The Maltese-resident population for 2004 was estimated to make up 97.0 per cent of the total resident population.<sup id="cite_ref-Demo2004_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Demo2004-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All censuses since 1842 have shown a slight excess of females over males. The 1901 and 1911 censuses came closest to recording a balance. The highest female-to-male ratio was reached in 1957 (1088:1000) but since then the ratio has dropped continuously. The 2005 census showed a 1013:1000 female-to-male ratio.
Population growth has slowed down, from +9.5 per cent between the 1985 and 1995 censuses, to +6.9 per cent between the 1995 and 2005 censuses (a yearly average of +0.7 per cent). The birth rate stood at 3860 (a decrease of 21.8 per cent from the 1995 census) and the death rate stood at 3025. Thus, there was a natural population increase of 835 (compared to +888 for 2004, of which over a hundred were foreign residents).<sup id="cite_ref-NSO_20060711_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSO_20060711-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valletta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Valletta.jpg/220px-Valletta.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Valletta.jpg/330px-Valletta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Valletta.jpg/440px-Valletta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valletta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>, Malta's capital city</div></div></div>
<p>The population's age composition is similar to the age structure prevalent in the EU. Since 1967 there was observed a trend indicating an ageing population, and is expected to continue in the foreseeable future. Malta's <a href="/wiki/Dependency_ratio" title="Dependency ratio">old-age-dependency-ratio</a> rose from 17.2 per cent in 1995 to 19.8 per cent in 2005, reasonably lower than the EU's 24.9 per cent average; 31.5 per cent of the Maltese population is aged under 25 (compared to the EU's 29.1 per cent); but the 50–64 age group constitutes 20.3 per cent of the population, significantly higher than the EU's 17.9 per cent. Malta's old-age-dependency-ratio is expected to continue rising steadily in the coming years.
</p><p>Maltese legislation recognises both civil and canonical (ecclesiastical) marriages. Annulments by the ecclesiastical and civil courts are unrelated and are not necessarily mutually endorsed. Malta voted in favour of divorce legislation in a referendum held on 28 May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Abortion in Malta is illegal. A person must be 16 to marry.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The number of brides aged under 25 decreased from 1471 in 1997 to 766 in 2005; while the number of grooms under 25 decreased from 823 to 311. There is a constant trend that females are more likely than males to marry young. In 2005 there were 51 brides aged between 16 and 19, compared to 8 grooms.<sup id="cite_ref-NSO_20060711_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NSO_20060711-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the end of 2007 the population of the Maltese Islands stood at 410,290 and is expected to reach 424,028 by 2025. At the moment,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (September 2015)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> females slightly outnumber males, making up 50.3 per cent of the population. The largest proportion of persons&#160;&#8211;&#32;7.5 per cent&#160;&#8211;&#32;were aged 25–29, while there were 7.3 per cent falling into each of the 45–49 and 55–59 age brackets.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> (TFR) as of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> was estimated at 1.53 children born/woman, which is below the replacement rate of 2.1.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, 25.8 per cent of births were to unmarried women.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in 2013 was estimated at 79.98 years (77.69 years male, 82.41 years female).<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Il-Kantilena.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Il-Kantilena.png/220px-Il-Kantilena.png" width="220" height="324" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Il-Kantilena.png/330px-Il-Kantilena.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Il-Kantilena.png/440px-Il-Kantilena.png 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Il-Kantilena.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Il-Kantilena" title="Il-Kantilena">Il-Kantilena</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Pietru_Caxaro" title="Pietru Caxaro">Pietru Caxaro</a>, the oldest text in <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese language</a>, 15th century</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Malta" title="Languages of Malta">Languages of Malta</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="#Education"> §&#160;Education</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese language</a> (<a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>: <i lang="mt">Malti</i>) is one of the two constitutional <a href="/wiki/Languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Languages">languages</a> of Malta, having become official, however, only in 1934, and being considered as the national language. Previously, <a href="/wiki/Sicilian_language" title="Sicilian language">Sicilian</a> was the official and cultural language of Malta from the 12th century, and <a href="/wiki/Tuscan_dialect" title="Tuscan dialect">Tuscan dialect</a> of <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> from the 16th century. Alongside Maltese, English is also an official language of the country and hence the laws of the land are enacted both in Maltese and English. However, article 74 of the Constitution states that "... if there is any conflict between the Maltese and the English texts of any law, the Maltese text shall prevail."<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Maltese is a <a href="/wiki/Semitic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Semitic language">Semitic language</a> descended from the now defunct Sicilian-Arabic (<a href="/wiki/Siculo-Arabic" title="Siculo-Arabic">Siculo-Arabic</a>) dialect (from <a href="/wiki/Southern_Italy" title="Southern Italy">southern Italy</a>) that developed during the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Sicily" title="Emirate of Sicily">Emirate of Sicily</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MED_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Maltese_alphabet" title="Maltese alphabet">Maltese alphabet</a> consists of 30 letters based on the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">diacritically</a> altered letters <i><a href="/wiki/%C5%BB" title="Ż">ż</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C4%8A" title="Ċ">ċ</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/%C4%A0" title="Ġ">ġ</a></i>, as well as the letters <i><a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7" class="mw-redirect" title="Għ">għ</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/%C4%A6" class="mw-redirect" title="Ħ">ħ</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Ie_(digraph)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ie (digraph)">ie</a></i>.
</p><p>Maltese has a Semitic base with substantial borrowing from <a href="/wiki/Sicilian_language" title="Sicilian language">Sicilian</a>, Italian, a little French, and more recently and increasingly, English.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> The hybrid character of Maltese was established by a long period of Maltese-Sicilian urban bilingualism gradually transforming rural speech and which ended in the early 19th century with Maltese emerging as the vernacular of the entire native population. The language includes different dialects that can vary greatly from one town to another or from one island to another.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> states that 97% per cent of the Maltese population consider Maltese as mother tongue. Also, 88 per cent of the population speak English, 66 per cent speak Italian, and 17 per cent speak French.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> This widespread knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Second_language" title="Second language">second languages</a> makes Malta one of the most multilingual countries in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. A study collecting public opinion on what language was "preferred" discovered that 86 per cent of the population express a preference for Maltese, 12 per cent for English, and 2 per cent for Italian.<sup id="cite_ref-LinguisticView_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LinguisticView-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Still, Italian television channels from Italy-based broadcasters, such as <a href="/wiki/Mediaset" title="Mediaset">Mediaset</a> and <a href="/wiki/RAI" title="RAI">RAI</a>, reach Malta and remain popular.<sup id="cite_ref-LinguisticView_209-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LinguisticView-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Domen_i_Mosta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Domen_i_Mosta.jpg/220px-Domen_i_Mosta.jpg" width="220" height="189" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Domen_i_Mosta.jpg/330px-Domen_i_Mosta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Domen_i_Mosta.jpg/440px-Domen_i_Mosta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1754" data-file-height="1504" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Domen_i_Mosta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Rotunda_of_Mosta" title="Rotunda of Mosta">Mosta Dome</a> known as "Ir-Rotunda"</div></div></div>
<table class="toccolours" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em; font-size: 85%; background:#c6dbf7; color:black; width:30em; max-width: 40%;" cellspacing="5">

<td style="text-align: left;"><i>(1) The religion of Malta is the Roman Catholic apostolic religion.<br /> (2) The authorities of the Roman Catholic apostolic church have the duty and the right to teach which principles are right and which are wrong.<br /> (3) Religious teaching of the Roman Catholic apostolic faith shall be provided in all state schools as part of compulsory education.</i>
</td></tr>

<td style="text-align: left;">Chapter 1, Article 2 of the Constitution of Malta<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<p>Religion in Malta (2016)<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholicism</a> (88.6%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:MediumTurquoise; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> (0.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:CornflowerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Christian (0.8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Aqua; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<abbr title="Believe in God without religion">Only believe in God</abbr> (1.8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (2.6%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other religions (1.3%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Gray; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">Atheists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">non-religious</a> (4.5%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Malta" title="Religion in Malta">Religion in Malta</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Malta" title="History of the Jews in Malta">History of the Jews in Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Malta" title="Christianity in Malta">Christianity in Malta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Malta" title="Islam in Malta">Islam in Malta</a></div>
<p>The predominant religion in Malta is <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholicism</a>. The second article of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Malta" title="Constitution of Malta">Constitution of Malta</a> establishes Catholicism as the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a> and it is also reflected in various elements of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Malta" title="Culture of Malta">Maltese culture</a>, although <a href="/wiki/Entrenched_clause" title="Entrenched clause">entrenched provisions</a> for the freedom of religion are made.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are more than 360 churches in Malta, Gozo and Comino, or one church for every 1,000 residents. The parish church (Maltese: <i>"il-parroċċa"</i>, or <i>"il-knisja parrokkjali"</i>) is the architectural and geographic focal point of every Maltese town and village, and its main source of civic pride. This civic pride manifests itself in spectacular fashion during the local village <i>festas</i>, which mark the day of the patron saint of each parish with marching bands, religious processions, special <a href="/wiki/Holy_Mass" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Mass">Masses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">fireworks</a> (especially petards) and other festivities.
</p><p>Malta is an <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_See" class="mw-redirect" title="Apostolic See">Apostolic See</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_the_Apostles" title="Acts of the Apostles">Acts of the Apostles</a> tells of how <a href="/wiki/Paul_of_Tarsus" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul of Tarsus">St. Paul</a>, on his way from Jerusalem to Rome to face trial, was shipwrecked on the island of "Melite", which many Bible scholars identify with Malta, an episode dated around AD 60.<sup id="cite_ref-doi.gov.mt_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doi.gov.mt-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> As recorded in the Acts of the Apostles, St. Paul spent three months on the island on his way to Rome, curing the sick including the father of Publius, the "chief man of the island". Various traditions are associated with this account. The shipwreck is said to have occurred in the place today known as <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="St Paul&#39;s Bay">St Paul's Bay</a>. The Maltese saint, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Publius" title="Saint Publius">Saint Publius</a> is said to have been made Malta's first bishop and a grotto in <a href="/wiki/Rabat,_Malta" title="Rabat, Malta">Rabat</a>, now known as "St Paul's Grotto" (and in the vicinity of which evidence of Christian burials and rituals from the 3rd century AD has been found), is among the earliest known places of Christian worship on the island.
</p><p>Further evidence of Christian practices and beliefs during the period of Roman persecution appears in <a href="/wiki/Catacombs" title="Catacombs">catacombs</a> that lie beneath various sites around Malta, including St Paul's Catacombs and St Agatha's Catacombs in Rabat, just outside the walls of <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">Mdina</a>. The latter, in particular, were beautifully frescoed between 1200 and 1480, although marauding <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Turks</a> defaced many of them in the 1550s. There are also a number of cave churches, including the grotto at <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_Our_Lady_of_Mellie%C4%A7a" title="Sanctuary of Our Lady of Mellieħa">Mellieħa</a>, which is a Shrine of the Nativity of Our Lady where, according to legend, <a href="/wiki/St._Luke" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Luke">St. Luke</a> painted a picture of the <a href="/wiki/The_Madonna" class="mw-redirect" title="The Madonna">Madonna</a>. It has been a place of pilgrimage since <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> times.
</p><p>The Acts of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Chalcedon" title="Council of Chalcedon">Council of Chalcedon</a> record that in 451 AD a certain Acacius was Bishop of Malta (<i>Melitenus Episcopus</i>). It is also known that in 501 AD, a certain Constantinus, <i>Episcopus Melitenensis</i>, was present at the <a href="/wiki/Second_Council_of_Constantinople" title="Second Council of Constantinople">Fifth Ecumenical Council</a>. In 588 AD, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_I" title="Pope Gregory I">Pope Gregory I</a> deposed Tucillus, <i>Miletinae civitatis episcopus</i> and the clergy and people of Malta elected his successor Trajan in 599 AD. The last recorded Bishop of Malta before the invasion of the islands was a Greek named Manas, who was subsequently incarcerated at <a href="/wiki/Palermo" title="Palermo">Palermo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Maltese historian <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Francesco_Abela" title="Giovanni Francesco Abela">Giovanni Francesco Abela</a> states that following their conversion to Christianity at the hand of <a href="/wiki/Saul_of_Tarsus" class="mw-redirect" title="Saul of Tarsus">St. Paul</a>, the Maltese retained their Christian religion, despite the <a href="/wiki/Fatimid" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimid">Fatimid</a> invasion.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Abela's writings describe Malta as a divinely ordained "bulwark of Christian, European civilization against the spread of Mediterranean Islam".<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The native Christian community that welcomed <a href="/wiki/Roger_I_of_Sicily" title="Roger I of Sicily">Roger I of Sicily</a><sup id="cite_ref-malticross_31-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malticross-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> was further bolstered by immigration to Malta from Italy, in the 12th and 13th centuries.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ZTN_city_center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/ZTN_city_center.jpg/220px-ZTN_city_center.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/ZTN_city_center.jpg/330px-ZTN_city_center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/ZTN_city_center.jpg/440px-ZTN_city_center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="345" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ZTN_city_center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/%C5%BBejtun" title="Żejtun">Żejtun</a> city centre parish church</div></div></div>
<p>For centuries, the Church in Malta was subordinate to the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Palermo" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Palermo">Diocese of Palermo</a>, except when it was under <a href="/wiki/Charles_of_Anjou" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles of Anjou">Charles of Anjou</a>, who appointed bishops for Malta, as did&#160;– on rare occasions&#160;– the Spanish and later, the Knights. Since 1808 all bishops of Malta have been Maltese. As a result of the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Malta#Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="History of Malta">Norman</a> and Spanish periods, and the rule of the Knights, Malta became the devout Catholic nation that it is today. It is worth noting that the Office of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Inquisition" title="Roman Inquisition">Inquisitor of Malta</a> had a very long tenure on the island following its establishment in 1530: the last Inquisitor departed from the Islands in 1798, after the Knights capitulated to the forces of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a>. During the period of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Venice" title="Republic of Venice">Republic of Venice</a>, several Maltese families emigrated to <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>. Their descendants account for about two-thirds of the community of some 4,000 Catholics that now live on that island.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Saint_George_in_Valletta.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Saint_George_in_Valletta.jpeg/220px-Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Saint_George_in_Valletta.jpeg" width="220" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Saint_George_in_Valletta.jpeg/330px-Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Saint_George_in_Valletta.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Saint_George_in_Valletta.jpeg/440px-Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Saint_George_in_Valletta.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2538" data-file-height="3328" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Greek_Orthodox_Church_of_Saint_George_in_Valletta.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Greek Orthodox church of St. Georg in Valletta</div></div></div>
<p>The patron saints of Malta are <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">Saint Paul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Publius" title="Saint Publius">Saint Publius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agatha_of_Sicily" title="Agatha of Sicily">Saint Agatha</a>. Although not a patron saint, <a href="/wiki/George_Preca" title="George Preca">St George Preca</a> (San Ġorġ Preca) is greatly revered as the second canonised Maltese saint after <a href="/wiki/St._Publius" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Publius">St. Publius</a> Malta's first acknowledged saint (canonised in the year 1634). <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> canonised him on 3 June 2007. Also, a number of Maltese individuals are recognised as <a href="/wiki/Beatification" title="Beatification">Blessed</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Maria_Adeodata_Pisani" title="Maria Adeodata Pisani">Maria Adeodata Pisani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nazju_Falzon" title="Nazju Falzon">Nazju Falzon</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> having <a href="/wiki/Beatified" class="mw-redirect" title="Beatified">beatified</a> them in 2001.
</p><p>Various Catholic religious orders are present in Malta, including the <a href="/wiki/Jesuits" class="mw-redirect" title="Jesuits">Jesuits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franciscans" title="Franciscans">Franciscans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">Dominicans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Little_Sisters_of_the_Poor" title="Little Sisters of the Poor">Little Sisters of the Poor</a>.
</p><p>Most congregants of the local <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> churches are not Maltese; their congregations draw on the many British retirees living in the country and vacationers from many other nations. There are approximately 600 <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> (LDS Church), the Bible Baptist Church, and the <a href="/wiki/Fellowship_of_Evangelical_Churches" title="Fellowship of Evangelical Churches">Fellowship of Evangelical Churches</a> each have about 60 affiliates. There are also some churches of other denominations, including <a href="/wiki/St._Andrew%27s_Scots_Church,_Malta" title="St. Andrew&#39;s Scots Church, Malta">St. Andrew's Scots Church</a> in Valletta (a joint <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian" class="mw-redirect" title="Presbyterian">Presbyterian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church_of_Great_Britain" title="Methodist Church of Great Britain">Methodist</a> congregation) and <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Anglican_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="St Paul&#39;s Anglican Cathedral">St Paul's Anglican Cathedral</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist</a> church in <a href="/wiki/Birkirkara" title="Birkirkara">Birkirkara</a>. A <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Church</a> congregation was founded in 1983 in Gwardamangia.<sup id="cite_ref-archive.maltatoday.com.mt_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive.maltatoday.com.mt-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Jewish population of Malta reached its peak in the Middle Ages under Norman rule. In 1479, Malta and <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> came under <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Aragonese</a> rule and the <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">Alhambra Decree</a> of 1492 forced all Jews to leave the country, permitting them to take with them only a few of their belongings. Several dozen Maltese Jews may have <a href="/wiki/Religious_conversion" title="Religious conversion">converted</a> to Christianity at the time to remain in the country. Today, there is one Jewish congregation.<sup id="cite_ref-archive.maltatoday.com.mt_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive.maltatoday.com.mt-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_Paola_-_Triq_Kordin_-_Mosque_07_ies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Malta_-_Paola_-_Triq_Kordin_-_Mosque_07_ies.jpg/220px-Malta_-_Paola_-_Triq_Kordin_-_Mosque_07_ies.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Malta_-_Paola_-_Triq_Kordin_-_Mosque_07_ies.jpg/330px-Malta_-_Paola_-_Triq_Kordin_-_Mosque_07_ies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Malta_-_Paola_-_Triq_Kordin_-_Mosque_07_ies.jpg/440px-Malta_-_Paola_-_Triq_Kordin_-_Mosque_07_ies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_Paola_-_Triq_Kordin_-_Mosque_07_ies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mariam_Al-Batool_Mosque" title="Mariam Al-Batool Mosque">Mariam Al-Batool Mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paola,_Malta" title="Paola, Malta">Paola, Malta</a></div></div></div>
<p>There is one Muslim mosque, the <a href="/wiki/Mariam_Al-Batool_Mosque" title="Mariam Al-Batool Mosque">Mariam Al-Batool Mosque</a>. A Muslim primary school recently opened. Of the estimated 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Malta" title="Islam in Malta">Muslims in Malta</a>, approximately 2,250 are foreigners, approximately 600 are naturalised citizens, and approximately 150 are native-born Maltese.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Zen_Buddhism" class="mw-redirect" title="Zen Buddhism">Zen Buddhism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bahá&#39;í Faith">Bahá'í Faith</a> claim some 40 members.<sup id="cite_ref-archive.maltatoday.com.mt_218-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive.maltatoday.com.mt-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a survey held by the <a href="/wiki/Malta_Today" title="Malta Today">Malta Today</a>, it was found that approximately 4.5 per cent of the population of Malta gives no preference to any religious belief. The number of <a href="/wiki/Atheists" class="mw-redirect" title="Atheists">Atheists</a> has exponentially grown, by doubling from 2014 to 2016. <a href="/wiki/Non-religious" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-religious">Non-religious</a> people have a higher risk to suffer from discrimination, such as lack of trust by society and unequal treatment by institutions. In the 2015 edition of the annual <a href="/wiki/International_Humanist_and_Ethical_Union#The_Freedom_of_Thought_Report" title="International Humanist and Ethical Union">Freedom of Thought Report</a> from the <a href="/wiki/International_Humanist_and_Ethical_Union" title="International Humanist and Ethical Union">International Humanist and Ethical Union</a>, Malta was in the category of "severe discrimination". In 2016, following the <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy_law#Malta" title="Blasphemy law">abolishment of blasphemy law</a>, Malta was shifted to the category of "systematic discrimination" (which is the same category as most EU countries).<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Inbound_migration">Inbound migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Inbound migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="toc" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="width:25%; float:right; text-align:center; clear:all; margin-left:8px; font-size:90%;">

<tbody><tr>
