<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Malta" title="Immigration to Malta">Immigration to Malta</a></div>
<p>Most of the foreign community in Malta, predominantly active or retired British nationals and their dependents, is centred on <a href="/wiki/Sliema" title="Sliema">Sliema</a> and surrounding modern suburbs. Other smaller foreign groups include Italians, Libyans and Serbians, many of whom have assimilated into the Maltese nation over the decades.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the late 20th century, Malta has become a transit country for migration routes from Africa towards Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Schengen agreement">Schengen agreement</a>, Malta is bound by the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Regulation" title="Dublin Regulation">Dublin Regulation</a> to process all claims for asylum by those asylum seekers that enter EU territory for the first time in Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Irregular migrants who land in Malta are subject to a <a href="/wiki/Immigration_detention" title="Immigration detention">compulsory detention policy</a>, being held in several camps organised by the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Malta" title="Armed Forces of Malta">Armed Forces of Malta</a> (AFM), including those near <a href="/wiki/%C4%A6al_Far" title="Ħal Far">Ħal Far</a> and <a href="/wiki/Safi,_Malta" title="Safi, Malta">Ħal Safi</a>. The compulsory detention policy has been denounced by several NGOs, and in July 2010, the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a> found that Malta's detention of migrants was arbitrary, lacking in adequate procedures to challenge detention, and in breach of its obligations under the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2014 Malta started granting citizenship for a €650,000 contribution plus investments, contingent on residence and criminal background requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Outbound_migration">Outbound migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Outbound migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_Floriana_-_Valletta_Waterfront_-_Laguna_Marina_-_Child_Migrants%27_Memorial_03_ies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Malta_-_Floriana_-_Valletta_Waterfront_-_Laguna_Marina_-_Child_Migrants%27_Memorial_03_ies.jpg/220px-Malta_-_Floriana_-_Valletta_Waterfront_-_Laguna_Marina_-_Child_Migrants%27_Memorial_03_ies.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Malta_-_Floriana_-_Valletta_Waterfront_-_Laguna_Marina_-_Child_Migrants%27_Memorial_03_ies.jpg/330px-Malta_-_Floriana_-_Valletta_Waterfront_-_Laguna_Marina_-_Child_Migrants%27_Memorial_03_ies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Malta_-_Floriana_-_Valletta_Waterfront_-_Laguna_Marina_-_Child_Migrants%27_Memorial_03_ies.jpg/440px-Malta_-_Floriana_-_Valletta_Waterfront_-_Laguna_Marina_-_Child_Migrants%27_Memorial_03_ies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_Floriana_-_Valletta_Waterfront_-_Laguna_Marina_-_Child_Migrants%27_Memorial_03_ies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Child Migrants' Memorial at the <a href="/wiki/Valletta_Waterfront" title="Valletta Waterfront">Valletta Waterfront</a>, commemorating the 310 child migrants who travelled to Australia between 1950 and 1965</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Emigration_from_Malta" title="Emigration from Malta">Emigration from Malta</a></div>
<p>In the 19th century, most emigration from Malta was to North Africa and the Middle East, although rates of <a href="/wiki/Repatriation" title="Repatriation">return migration</a> to Malta were high.<sup id="cite_ref-Jones_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, Maltese communities formed in these regions. By 1900, for example, British consular estimates suggest that there were 15,326 Maltese in <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, and in 1903 it was claimed that 15,000 people of Maltese origin were living in <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Attard_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Attard-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta experienced significant emigration as a result of the collapse of a construction boom in 1907 and after the Second World War, when the <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> increased significantly, but in the 20th century most emigrants went to destinations in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>, particularly to Australia, Canada and the United States. After the Second World War, Malta's Emigration Department would assist emigrants with the cost of their travel. Between 1948 and 1967, 30 per cent of the population emigrated.<sup id="cite_ref-Jones_227-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Between 1946 and the late-1970s, over 140,000 people left Malta on the assisted passage scheme, with 57.6% migrating to Australia, 22% to the UK, 13% to Canada and 7% to the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-King_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-King-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Emigration dropped dramatically after the mid-1970s and has since ceased to be a social phenomenon of significance. However, since Malta joined the EU in 2004 <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriate</a> communities emerged in a number of European countries particularly in <a href="/wiki/Maltese_in_Belgium" title="Maltese in Belgium">Belgium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Malta" title="Education in Malta">Education in Malta</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Malta" title="List of schools in Malta">List of schools in Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Uni-20malta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Uni-20malta.jpg/220px-Uni-20malta.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Uni-20malta.jpg/330px-Uni-20malta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Uni-20malta.jpg/440px-Uni-20malta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Uni-20malta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/University_of_Malta" title="University of Malta">University of Malta</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bibliothek_in_Malta,_in_Valletta.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Bibliothek_in_Malta%2C_in_Valletta.JPG/220px-Bibliothek_in_Malta%2C_in_Valletta.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Bibliothek_in_Malta%2C_in_Valletta.JPG/330px-Bibliothek_in_Malta%2C_in_Valletta.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Bibliothek_in_Malta%2C_in_Valletta.JPG/440px-Bibliothek_in_Malta%2C_in_Valletta.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bibliothek_in_Malta,_in_Valletta.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Library in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a></div></div></div>
<p>Primary schooling has been compulsory since 1946; secondary education up to the age of sixteen was made compulsory in 1971. The state and the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Church</a> provide education free of charge, both running a number of schools in Malta and <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>, including <a href="/wiki/De_La_Salle_College_(Malta)" title="De La Salle College (Malta)">De La Salle College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cospicua" title="Cospicua">Cospicua</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Aloysius%27_College_(Malta)" title="St Aloysius&#39; College (Malta)">St. Aloysius' College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Birkirkara" title="Birkirkara">Birkirkara</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Paul%27s_Missionary_College" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Paul&#39;s Missionary College">St. Paul's Missionary College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rabat,_Malta" title="Rabat, Malta">Rabat, Malta</a>, St. Joseph's School in <a href="/wiki/Blata_l-Bajda" title="Blata l-Bajda">Blata l-Bajda</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Malta" title="List of schools in Malta">Saint Monica Girls' School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mosta" title="Mosta">Mosta</a>. As of  2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, state schools are organised into networks known as Colleges and incorporate kindergarten schools, primary and secondary schools. A number of private schools are run in Malta, including <a href="/wiki/San_Andrea_School" title="San Andrea School">San Andrea School</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Anton_School" title="San Anton School">San Anton School</a> in the valley of L-Imselliet (l/o <a href="/wiki/M%C4%A1arr" title="Mġarr">Mġarr</a>), <a href="/wiki/St._Martin%27s_College" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Martin&#39;s College">St. Martin's College</a> in Swatar and St. Michael's School in <a href="/wiki/San_%C4%A0wann" title="San Ġwann">San Ġwann</a>. St. Catherine's High School, Pembroke offers an International Foundation Course for students wishing to learn English before entering mainstream education. As of  2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there are two international schools, Verdala International School and QSI Malta. The state pays a portion of the teachers' salary in Church schools.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Education in Malta is based on the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Education in the United Kingdom">British model</a>. Primary school lasts six years. At the age of 11 pupils sit for an examination to enter a secondary school, either a <a href="/wiki/Church_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Church school">church school</a> (the Common Entrance Examination) or a <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">state school</a>. Pupils sit for SEC <a href="/wiki/O-level" class="mw-redirect" title="O-level">O-level</a> examinations at the age of 16, with passes obligatory in certain subjects such as mathematics, English and <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>. Pupils may opt to continue studying at a <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form_college" title="Sixth form college">sixth form college</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Gan_Frangisk_Abela_Junior_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Gan Frangisk Abela Junior College">Gan Frangisk Abela Junior College</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Aloysius%27_College_(Malta)" title="St Aloysius&#39; College (Malta)">St. Aloysius' College</a>, Giovanni Curmi Higher Secondary, <a href="/wiki/De_La_Salle_College_(Malta)" title="De La Salle College (Malta)">De La Salle College</a>, St Edward's College, or else at another post-secondary institution such as <a href="/wiki/MCAST" class="mw-redirect" title="MCAST">MCAST</a>. The sixth form course lasts for two years, at the end of which students sit for the Matriculation examination. Subject to their performance, students may then apply for an undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degree</a> or diploma.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Malta" title="University of Malta">University of Malta</a> (U.o.M.) provides Tertiary education at diploma, undergraduate and postgraduate level. The adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Literacy rate">literacy rate</a> is 99.5 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Maltese and English are both used to teach pupils at primary and secondary school level, and both languages are also compulsory subjects. <a href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" class="mw-redirect" title="Public school (government funded)">Public schools</a> tend to use both Maltese and English in a balanced manner. Private schools prefer to use English for teaching, as is also the case with most departments of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Malta" title="University of Malta">University of Malta</a>; this has a limiting effect on the capacity and development of the Maltese language.<sup id="cite_ref-LinguisticView_209-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LinguisticView-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Most university courses are in English.<sup id="cite_ref-MED_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MED-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since September 2015">dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup>
</p><p>Of the total number of pupils studying a first foreign language at secondary level, 51 per cent take Italian whilst 38 per cent take French. Other choices include German, Russian, Spanish, Latin, Chinese and Arabic.<sup id="cite_ref-LinguisticView_209-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LinguisticView-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since September 2015">dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta is also a popular destination to study the English language, attracting over 80,000 students in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Malta" title="Healthcare in Malta">Healthcare in Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_Valletta_-_Triq_il-Mediterran-Triq_it-Tramuntana_-_Mediterranean_Conference_Centre_01_ies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Malta_-_Valletta_-_Triq_il-Mediterran-Triq_it-Tramuntana_-_Mediterranean_Conference_Centre_01_ies.jpg/220px-Malta_-_Valletta_-_Triq_il-Mediterran-Triq_it-Tramuntana_-_Mediterranean_Conference_Centre_01_ies.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Malta_-_Valletta_-_Triq_il-Mediterran-Triq_it-Tramuntana_-_Mediterranean_Conference_Centre_01_ies.jpg/330px-Malta_-_Valletta_-_Triq_il-Mediterran-Triq_it-Tramuntana_-_Mediterranean_Conference_Centre_01_ies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Malta_-_Valletta_-_Triq_il-Mediterran-Triq_it-Tramuntana_-_Mediterranean_Conference_Centre_01_ies.jpg/440px-Malta_-_Valletta_-_Triq_il-Mediterran-Triq_it-Tramuntana_-_Mediterranean_Conference_Centre_01_ies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_-_Valletta_-_Triq_il-Mediterran-Triq_it-Tramuntana_-_Mediterranean_Conference_Centre_01_ies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Sacra Infermeria was used as a hospital from the 16th to 20th centuries. It is now the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Conference_Centre" title="Mediterranean Conference Centre">Mediterranean Conference Centre</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mater_Dei_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Mater_Dei_01.jpg/220px-Mater_Dei_01.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Mater_Dei_01.jpg/330px-Mater_Dei_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Mater_Dei_01.jpg/440px-Mater_Dei_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4347" data-file-height="2898" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mater_Dei_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mater_Dei_Hospital" title="Mater Dei Hospital">Mater Dei Hospital</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MMSA_Checking_Blood_Pressure.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/MMSA_Checking_Blood_Pressure.JPG/220px-MMSA_Checking_Blood_Pressure.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/MMSA_Checking_Blood_Pressure.JPG/330px-MMSA_Checking_Blood_Pressure.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/13/MMSA_Checking_Blood_Pressure.JPG/440px-MMSA_Checking_Blood_Pressure.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MMSA_Checking_Blood_Pressure.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Medical Student taking blood pressure during an event organised by the local medical student association</div></div></div>
<p>Malta has a long history of providing <a href="/wiki/Publicly_funded_health_care" title="Publicly funded health care">publicly funded health care</a>. The first hospital recorded in the country was already functioning by 1372.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
Today, Malta has both a public healthcare system, known as the government healthcare service, where healthcare is free at the point of delivery, and a <a href="/wiki/Private_healthcare" title="Private healthcare">private healthcare</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> Malta has a strong general practitioner-delivered primary care base and the public hospitals provide secondary and tertiary care. The Maltese Ministry of Health advises foreign residents to take out private medical insurance.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Malta also boasts voluntary organisations such as Alpha Medical (Advanced Care), the Emergency Fire &amp; Rescue Unit (E.F.R.U.), St John Ambulance and Red Cross Malta who provide first aid/nursing services during events involving crowds.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Mater_Dei_Hospital" title="Mater Dei Hospital">Mater Dei Hospital</a>, Malta's primary hospital, opened in 2007. It has one of the largest medical buildings in Europe.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Malta" title="University of Malta">University of Malta</a> has a <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a> and a Faculty of <a href="/wiki/Health_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Health Sciences">Health Sciences</a>, the latter offering diploma, degree (BSc) and postgraduate degree courses in a number of health care disciplines.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Medical_Association_of_Malta" title="Medical Association of Malta">Medical Association of Malta</a> represents practitioners of the medical profession. The <a href="/wiki/Malta_Medical_Students%27_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Malta Medical Students&#39; Association">Malta Medical Students' Association</a> (MMSA) is a separate body representing Maltese medical students, and is a member of <a href="/wiki/European_Medical_Students%27_Association" title="European Medical Students&#39; Association">EMSA</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Medical_Students%27_Associations" title="International Federation of Medical Students&#39; Associations">IFMSA</a>. <a href="/wiki/Malta_Institute_for_Medical_Education" title="Malta Institute for Medical Education">MIME</a>, the Maltese Institute for Medical Education, is an institute set up recently to provide CME to physicians in Malta as well as medical students. The <a href="/wiki/Foundation_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="Foundation Program">Foundation Program</a> followed in the UK has been introduced in Malta to stem the 'brain drain' of newly graduated physicians to the British Isles. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta_Association_of_Dental_Students&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Malta Association of Dental Students (page does not exist)">Malta Association of Dental Students</a> (MADS) is a student association set up to promote the rights of Dental Surgery Students studying within the faculty of Dental Surgery of the University of Malta. It is affiliated with <a href="/w/index.php?title=IADS&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="IADS (page does not exist)">IADS</a>, the International Association of Dental Students.
</p><p>See also <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Malta" title="Health in Malta">Health in Malta</a>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Malta" title="Culture of Malta">Culture of Malta</a></div>
<p>The culture of Malta reflects the various cultures, from the Phoenicians to the British, that have come into contact with the Maltese Islands throughout the centuries, including neighbouring Mediterranean cultures, and the cultures of the nations that ruled Malta for long periods of time prior to its <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Malta)" title="Independence Day (Malta)">independence</a> in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Malta" title="Music of Malta">Music of Malta</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manoel_theatre_(12851453033).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Manoel_theatre_%2812851453033%29.jpg/220px-Manoel_theatre_%2812851453033%29.jpg" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Manoel_theatre_%2812851453033%29.jpg/330px-Manoel_theatre_%2812851453033%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Manoel_theatre_%2812851453033%29.jpg/440px-Manoel_theatre_%2812851453033%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="649" data-file-height="347" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manoel_theatre_(12851453033).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Manoel_Theatre" title="Manoel Theatre">Manoel Theatre</a>, Europe's third-oldest working theatre. Now Malta's National Theatre and home to the <a href="/wiki/Malta_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Malta Philharmonic Orchestra">Malta Philharmonic Orchestra</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>While Maltese music today is largely Western, traditional Maltese music includes what is known as <a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7ana_(folk_music)" title="Għana (folk music)">għana</a>. This consists of background <a href="/wiki/Folk_guitar" class="mw-redirect" title="Folk guitar">folk guitar</a> music, while a few people, generally men, take it in turns to argue a point in a sing-song voice. The aim of the lyrics, which are improvised, is to create a friendly yet challenging atmosphere, and it takes a number of years of practice to be able to combine the required artistic qualities with the ability to <a href="/wiki/Debate" title="Debate">debate</a> effectively.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maltese_literature" title="Maltese literature">Maltese literature</a></div>
<p>Documented Maltese literature is over 200 years old. However, a recently unearthed love ballad testifies to literary activity in the local tongue from the Medieval period. Malta followed a Romantic literary tradition, culminating in the works of <a href="/wiki/Dun_Karm_Psaila" title="Dun Karm Psaila">Dun Karm Psaila</a>, Malta's National Poet. Subsequent writers like <a href="/wiki/Ruzar_Briffa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ruzar Briffa">Ruzar Briffa</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Karmenu_Vassallo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Karmenu Vassallo (page does not exist)">Karmenu Vassallo</a> tried to estrange themselves from the rigidity of formal themes and versification.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The next generation of writers, including <a href="/wiki/Karl_Schembri" title="Karl Schembri">Karl Schembri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Mifsud" title="Immanuel Mifsud">Immanuel Mifsud</a>, widened the tracks further, especially in prose and poetry.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:San_Giulian,_Marina.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/San_Giulian%2C_Marina.jpg/220px-San_Giulian%2C_Marina.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/San_Giulian%2C_Marina.jpg/330px-San_Giulian%2C_Marina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/San_Giulian%2C_Marina.jpg/440px-San_Giulian%2C_Marina.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:San_Giulian,_Marina.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical architecture built in recent years in Malta</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Art and architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vallettaupperbarraccagardens.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Vallettaupperbarraccagardens.JPG/220px-Vallettaupperbarraccagardens.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Vallettaupperbarraccagardens.JPG/330px-Vallettaupperbarraccagardens.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Vallettaupperbarraccagardens.JPG/440px-Vallettaupperbarraccagardens.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vallettaupperbarraccagardens.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lower Barrakka Gardens</div></div></div>
<p>Maltese architecture has been influenced by many different Mediterranean cultures and British architecture over its history. The first settlers on the island constructed <a href="/wiki/%C4%A0gantija" title="Ġgantija">Ġgantija</a>, one of the oldest manmade freestanding structures in the world. The Neolithic temple builders 3800–2500 BC endowed the numerous temples of Malta and Gozo with intricate bas relief designs, including spirals evocative of the tree of life and animal portraits, designs painted in red ochre, ceramics and a vast collection of human form sculptures, particularly the Venus of Malta. These can be viewed at the temples themselves (most notably, the <a href="/wiki/Hypogeum_of_%C4%A6al-Saflieni" class="mw-redirect" title="Hypogeum of Ħal-Saflieni">Hypogeum</a> and Tarxien Temples), and at the National Museum of Archaeology in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>. Malta's temples such as Imnajdra are full of history and have a story behind them. Malta is currently undergoing several large-scale building projects, including the construction of <a href="/wiki/SmartCity_Malta" title="SmartCity Malta">SmartCity Malta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/M-Towers" title="M-Towers">M-Towers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pendergardens" title="Pendergardens">Pendergardens</a>, while areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Valletta_Waterfront" title="Valletta Waterfront">Valletta Waterfront</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tign%C3%A9_Point" title="Tigné Point">Tigné Point</a> have been or are being renovated.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Roman period introduced highly decorative mosaic floors, marble colonnades and classical statuary, remnants of which are beautifully preserved and presented in the Roman Domus, a country villa just outside the walls of <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">Mdina</a>. The early Christian frescoes that decorate the <a href="/wiki/Catacombs" title="Catacombs">catacombs</a> beneath Malta reveal a propensity for eastern, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> tastes. These tastes continued to inform the endeavours of <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> Maltese artists, but they were increasingly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_art" title="Romanesque art">Romanesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Gothic" title="Southern Gothic">Southern Gothic</a> movements. Towards the end of the 15th century, Maltese artists, like their counterparts in neighbouring Sicily, came under the influence of the School of <a href="/wiki/Antonello_da_Messina" title="Antonello da Messina">Antonello da Messina</a>, which introduced <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> ideals and concepts to the decorative arts in Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-hopeandoptimism1_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hopeandoptimism1-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CaravaggioJeromeValletta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/CaravaggioJeromeValletta.jpg/220px-CaravaggioJeromeValletta.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/CaravaggioJeromeValletta.jpg/330px-CaravaggioJeromeValletta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/CaravaggioJeromeValletta.jpg/440px-CaravaggioJeromeValletta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1037" data-file-height="716" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CaravaggioJeromeValletta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Saint Jerome Writing, by Caravaggio. Held in St John's Co-Cathedral, Valletta.</div></div></div>
<p>The artistic heritage of Malta blossomed under the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights of St. John</a>, who brought Italian and Flemish <a href="/wiki/Mannerist" class="mw-redirect" title="Mannerist">Mannerist</a> painters to decorate their palaces and the churches of these islands, most notably, <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Perez_d%27Aleccio" class="mw-redirect" title="Matteo Perez d&#39;Aleccio">Matteo Perez d'Aleccio</a>, whose works appear in the <a href="/wiki/Grandmaster%27s_Palace_in_Valletta" class="mw-redirect" title="Grandmaster&#39;s Palace in Valletta">Magisterial Palace</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Co-Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s Co-Cathedral">Conventual Church of St. John</a> in Valletta, and Filippo Paladini, who was active in Malta from 1590 to 1595. For many years, Mannerism continued to inform the tastes and ideals of local Maltese artists.<sup id="cite_ref-hopeandoptimism1_240-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hopeandoptimism1-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The arrival in Malta of <a href="/wiki/Caravaggio" title="Caravaggio">Caravaggio</a>, who painted at least seven works during his 15-month stay on these islands, further revolutionised local art. Two of Caravaggio's most notable works, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beheading_of_Saint_John_the_Baptist_(Caravaggio)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Beheading of Saint John the Baptist (Caravaggio)">The Beheading of Saint John the Baptist</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Saint_Jerome_Writing_(Valletta)" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Jerome Writing (Valletta)">Saint Jerome Writing</a></i>, are on display in the <a href="/wiki/Oratory_(worship)" title="Oratory (worship)">Oratory</a> of the Conventual Church of St. John. His legacy is evident in the works of local artists Giulio Cassarino (1582–1637) and <a href="/wiki/Stefano_Erardi" title="Stefano Erardi">Stefano Erardi</a> (1630–1716). However, the <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> movement that followed was destined to have the most enduring impact on Maltese art and architecture. The glorious vault paintings of the celebrated Calabrese artist, <a href="/wiki/Mattia_Preti" title="Mattia Preti">Mattia Preti</a> transformed the severe, Mannerist interior of the Conventual Church St. John into a Baroque masterpiece. Preti spent the last 40 years of his life in Malta, where he created many of his finest works, now on display in the Museum of Fine Arts in <a href="/wiki/Valletta" title="Valletta">Valletta</a>. During this period, local sculptor <a href="/wiki/Melchiorre_Caf%C3%A0" title="Melchiorre Cafà">Melchior Gafà</a> (1639–1667) emerged as one of the top Baroque sculptors of the Roman School.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Siege_of_malta_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Siege_of_malta_3.jpg/220px-Siege_of_malta_3.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Siege_of_malta_3.jpg/330px-Siege_of_malta_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Siege_of_malta_3.jpg/440px-Siege_of_malta_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="459" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Siege_of_malta_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Siege of Malta&#160;– Flight of the Turks</i>, by Matteo Perez d'Aleccio</div></div></div>
<p>During the 17th and 18th century, <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">Neapolitan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">Rococo</a> influences emerged in the works of the Italian painters <a href="/wiki/Luca_Giordano" title="Luca Giordano">Luca Giordano</a> (1632–1705) and <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Solimena" title="Francesco Solimena">Francesco Solimena</a> (1657–1747), and these developments can be seen in the work of their Maltese contemporaries such as Giovanni Nicola Buhagiar (1698–1752) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Francesco_Zahra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Francesco Zahra (page does not exist)">Francesco Zahra</a> (1710–1773). The Rococo movement was greatly enhanced by the relocation to Malta of Antoine de Favray (1706–1798), who assumed the position of court painter to Grand Master Pinto in 1744.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Neo-classicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-classicism">Neo-classicism</a> made some inroads among local Maltese artists in the late-18th century, but this trend was reversed in the early 19th century, as the local Church authorities&#160;– perhaps in an effort to strengthen Catholic resolve against the perceived threat of Protestantism during the early days of British rule in Malta&#160;– favoured and avidly promoted the religious themes embraced by the <a href="/wiki/Nazarene_movement" title="Nazarene movement">Nazarene movement</a> of artists. <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romanticism</a>, tempered by the naturalism introduced to Malta by <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Cal%C3%AC" title="Giuseppe Calì">Giuseppe Calì</a>, informed the "salon" artists of the early 20th century, including Edward and Robert Caruana Dingli.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Parliament established the National School of Art in the 1920s. During the reconstruction period that followed the Second World War, the emergence of the "Modern Art Group", whose members included <a href="/w/index.php?title=Josef_Kalleya&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Josef Kalleya (page does not exist)">Josef Kalleya</a> (1898–1998), <a href="/wiki/George_Preca" title="George Preca">George Preca</a> (1909–1984), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Anton_Inglott&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Anton Inglott (page does not exist)">Anton Inglott</a> (1915–1945), <a href="/wiki/Emvin_Cremona" title="Emvin Cremona">Envin Cremona</a> (1919–1987), <a href="/wiki/Frank_Portelli" title="Frank Portelli">Frank Portelli</a> (b. 1922-2004), <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Camilleri_(artist)" title="Antoine Camilleri (artist)">Antoine Camilleri</a> (b. 1922-2005) and <a href="/wiki/Esprit_Barthet" title="Esprit Barthet">Esprit Barthet</a> (b. 1919-1999) greatly enhanced the local art scene. This group of forward-looking artists came together forming an influential pressure group known as the Modern Art Group. Together they forced the Maltese public to take seriously modern aesthetics and succeeded in playing a leading role in the renewal of Maltese art. Most of Malta's modern artists have in fact studied in Art institutions in England, or on the continent, leading to the explosive development of a wide spectrum of views and to a diversity of artistic expression that has remained characteristic of contemporary Maltese art.  In Valletta, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts,_Malta" title="National Museum of Fine Arts, Malta">National Museum of Fine Arts</a> features work from artists such as <a href="/wiki/H._Craig_Hanna" title="H. Craig Hanna">H. Craig Hanna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MaltaInd_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MaltaInd-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Maltese_cuisine" title="Maltese cuisine">Maltese cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Maltese_dishes" title="List of Maltese dishes">List of Maltese dishes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Pastizzi.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Malta_Pastizzi.JPG/170px-Malta_Pastizzi.JPG" width="170" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Malta_Pastizzi.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="230" data-file-height="230" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_Pastizzi.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Pastizzi" class="mw-redirect" title="Pastizzi">Pastizzi</a></i>, a typical Maltese snack</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_ftira.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Malta_ftira.JPG/170px-Malta_ftira.JPG" width="170" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Malta_ftira.JPG/255px-Malta_ftira.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Malta_ftira.JPG/340px-Malta_ftira.JPG 2x" data-file-width="361" data-file-height="283" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Malta_ftira.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Ftira" title="Ftira">Ftira</a></i>, a type of Maltese bread</div></div></div>
<p>Maltese cuisine shows strong Sicilian and English influences as well as influences of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_cuisine" title="Spanish cuisine">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maghreb_cuisine" title="Maghreb cuisine">Maghrebin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Proven%C3%A7al_cuisine" class="mw-redirect" title="Provençal cuisine">Provençal</a> cuisines. A number of regional variations, particularly with regards to Gozo, can be noted as well as seasonal variations associated with the seasonal availability of produce and Christian feasts (such as <a href="/wiki/Lent" title="Lent">Lent</a>, Easter and Christmas). Food has been important historically in the development of a national identity in particular the traditional <i>fenkata</i> (i.e., the eating of stewed or fried rabbit).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Customs">Customs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Customs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Maltese_folklore" title="Maltese folklore">Maltese folklore</a></div>
<p>A 2010 <a href="/wiki/Charities_Aid_Foundation" title="Charities Aid Foundation">Charities Aid Foundation</a> study found that the Maltese were the most generous people in the world, with 83% contributing to charity.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Maltese folktales include various stories about mysterious creatures and supernatural events. These were most comprehensively compiled by the scholar (and pioneer in Maltese <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeology</a>) <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Magri" title="Manuel Magri">Manwel Magri</a><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> in his core criticism "<i>Ħrejjef Missirijietna</i>" ("Fables from our Forefathers"). This collection of material inspired subsequent researchers and academics to gather traditional <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">tales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fable" title="Fable">fables</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legend" title="Legend">legends</a> from all over the Archipelago.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Magri's work also inspired a series of comic books (released by Klabb Kotba Maltin in 1984): the titles included <i>Bin is-Sultan Jiźźewweġ x-Xebba tat-Tronġiet Mewwija</i> and <i>Ir-Rjieħ</i>. Many of these stories have been popularly re-written as Children's literature by authors writing in <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>, such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trevor_%C5%BBahra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Trevor Żahra (page does not exist)">Trevor Żahra</a>. While giants, witches and dragons feature in many of the stories, some contain entirely Maltese creatures like the <a href="/wiki/Kaw_kaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Kaw kaw">Kaw kaw</a>, <a href="/wiki/Il-Bellieg%C4%A7a" class="mw-redirect" title="Il-Belliegħa">Il-Belliegħa</a> and <a href="/wiki/L-Im%C4%A7alla" class="mw-redirect" title="L-Imħalla">L-Imħalla</a> among others. The traditional Maltese obsession with maintaining spiritual (or ritual) purity<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> means that many of these creatures have the role of guarding forbidden or restricted areas and attacking individuals who broke the strict codes of conduct that characterised the island's pre-industrial society.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Traditional Maltese proverbs reveal a cultural importance of childbearing and fertility: "<i>iż-żwieġ mingħajr tarbija ma fihx tgawdija</i>" (a childless marriage cannot be a happy one). This is a belief that Malta shares with many other Mediterranean cultures. In Maltese folktales the local variant of the classic closing formula, "and they all lived happily ever after" is "<i>u għammru u tgħammru, u spiċċat</i>" (and they lived together, and they had children together, and the tale is finished).<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rural Malta shares in common with Mediterranean society a number of superstitions regarding fertility, menstruation and pregnancy, including the avoidance of cemeteries during the months leading up to childbirth, and avoiding the preparation of certain foods during menses. Pregnant women are encouraged to satisfy their <a href="/wiki/Food_craving" title="Food craving">cravings</a> for specific foods, out of fear that their unborn child will bear a representational birth mark (Maltese: <i>xewqa</i>, literally "desire" or "craving"). Maltese and Sicilian women also share certain traditions that are believed to predict the sex of an unborn child, such as the cycle of the moon on the anticipated date of birth, whether the baby is carried "high" or "low" during pregnancy, and the movement of a wedding ring, dangled on a string above the abdomen (sideways denoting a girl, back and forth denoting a boy).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Traditionally, Maltese newborns were baptised as promptly as possible, should the child die in infancy without receiving this vital Sacrament; and partly because according to Maltese (and Sicilian) folklore an unbaptised child is not yet a Christian, but "still a Turk". Traditional Maltese delicacies served at a baptismal feast include <i>biskuttini tal-magħmudija</i> (almond macaroons covered in white or pink icing), <i>it-torta tal-marmorata</i> (a spicy, heart-shaped tart of chocolate-flavoured almond paste), and a liqueur known as <i>rożolin</i>, made with rose petals, violets and almonds.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On a child's first birthday, in a tradition that still survives today, Maltese parents would organise a game known as <i>il-quċċija</i>, where a variety of symbolic objects would be randomly placed around the seated child. These may include a hard-boiled egg, a Bible, <a href="/wiki/Crucifix" title="Crucifix">crucifix</a> or <a href="/wiki/Rosary_beads" class="mw-redirect" title="Rosary beads">rosary beads</a>, a book, and so on. Whichever object the child shows most interest in is said to reveal the child's path and fortunes in adulthood.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Money refers to a rich future while a book expresses intelligence and a possible career as a teacher. Infants who select a pencil or pen will be writers. Choosing Bibles or rosary beads refers to a clerical or monastic life. If the child chooses a hard-boiled egg, it will have a long life and many children. More recent additions include calculators (refers to accounting), thread (fashion) and wooden spoons (cooking and a great appetite).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Maltesewedding.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4e/Maltesewedding.jpg/220px-Maltesewedding.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4e/Maltesewedding.jpg/330px-Maltesewedding.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4e/Maltesewedding.jpg/440px-Maltesewedding.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="317" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Maltesewedding.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Re-enactment of a traditional Maltese 18th century wedding</div></div></div>
<p>Traditional Maltese weddings featured the bridal party walking in procession beneath an ornate canopy, from the home of the bride's family to the parish church, with singers trailing behind serenading the bride and groom. The Maltese word for this custom is <i>il-ġilwa</i>. This custom along with many others has long since disappeared from the islands, in the face of modern practices.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>New wives would wear the <a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7onnella" title="Għonnella">għonnella</a>, a traditional item of Maltese clothing. However, it is no longer worn in modern Malta. Today's couples are married in churches or chapels in the village or town of their choice. The nuptials are usually followed by a lavish and joyous wedding reception, often including several hundred guests. Occasionally, couples will try to incorporate elements of the traditional Maltese wedding in their celebration. A resurgent interest in the traditional wedding was evident in May 2007, when thousands of Maltese and tourists attended a traditional Maltese wedding in the style of the 16th century, in the village of <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBurrieq" title="Żurrieq">Żurrieq</a>. This included <i>il-ġilwa</i>, which led the bride and groom to a wedding ceremony that took place on the <a href="/wiki/Parvis" class="mw-redirect" title="Parvis">parvis</a> of St. Andrew's Chapel. The reception that followed featured folklore music (<i><a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7ana" class="mw-redirect" title="Għana">għana</a></i>) and dancing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_statue_of_St._George_issuing_from_the_Basilica_on_the_third_Sunday_of_July.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_statue_of_St._George_issuing_from_the_Basilica_on_the_third_Sunday_of_July.jpg/220px-The_statue_of_St._George_issuing_from_the_Basilica_on_the_third_Sunday_of_July.jpg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_statue_of_St._George_issuing_from_the_Basilica_on_the_third_Sunday_of_July.jpg/330px-The_statue_of_St._George_issuing_from_the_Basilica_on_the_third_Sunday_of_July.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_statue_of_St._George_issuing_from_the_Basilica_on_the_third_Sunday_of_July.jpg/440px-The_statue_of_St._George_issuing_from_the_Basilica_on_the_third_Sunday_of_July.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1712" data-file-height="2288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_statue_of_St._George_issuing_from_the_Basilica_on_the_third_Sunday_of_July.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The statue of St. George at the <i>festa</i> of <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Gozo" title="Victoria, Gozo">Victoria, Gozo</a></div></div></div>
<p>Local festivals, similar to those in Southern Italy, are commonplace in Malta and Gozo, celebrating weddings, <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">christenings</a> and, most prominently, <a href="/wiki/Saints" class="mw-redirect" title="Saints">saints</a>' days, honouring the patron saint of the local parish. On saints' days, the <i>festa</i> reaches its apex with a <a href="/wiki/Mass_(liturgy)" title="Mass (liturgy)">High Mass</a> featuring a sermon on the life and achievements of the patron saint, after which a <a href="/wiki/Statue" title="Statue">statue</a> of the religious patron is taken around the local streets in solemn procession, with the faithful following in respectful prayer. The atmosphere of religious devotion quickly gives way to several days of celebration and revelry: band processions, <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">fireworks</a>, and late-night parties.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Maltese_Carnival" title="Maltese Carnival">Carnival</a> (Maltese: <i>il-karnival ta' Malta</i>) has had an important place on the cultural calendar after <a href="/wiki/Grand_Master_(order)" title="Grand Master (order)">Grand Master</a> <a href="/wiki/Piero_de_Ponte" title="Piero de Ponte">Piero de Ponte</a> introduced it to the islands in 1535. It is held during the week leading up to <a href="/wiki/Ash_Wednesday" title="Ash Wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>, and typically includes masked balls, fancy dress and grotesque mask competitions, lavish late-night parties, a colourful, ticker-tape parade of allegorical <a href="/wiki/Float_(parade)" title="Float (parade)">floats</a> presided over by King Carnival (Maltese: <i>ir-Re tal-Karnival</i>), marching bands and costumed revellers.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Holy_Week_in_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Week in Malta">Holy Week</a> (Maltese: <i>il-Ġimgħa Mqaddsa</i>) starts on <a href="/wiki/Palm_Sunday" title="Palm Sunday">Palm Sunday</a> (<i>Ħadd il-Palm</i>) and ends on <a href="/wiki/Easter_Sunday" class="mw-redirect" title="Easter Sunday">Easter Sunday</a> (<i>Ħadd il-Għid</i>). Numerous religious traditions, most of them inherited from one generation to the next, are part of the <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">paschal</a> celebrations in the Maltese Islands, honouring the death and resurrection of Jesus.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Mnarja, or l-Imnarja (pronounced <i>lim-nar-ya</i>) is one of the most important dates on the Maltese cultural calendar. Officially, it is a national festival dedicated to the feast of <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">Saints</a> <a href="/wiki/St._Peter" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Peter">Peter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saul_of_Tarsus" class="mw-redirect" title="Saul of Tarsus">St. Paul</a>. Its roots can be traced back to the pagan <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman</a> feast of <i>Luminaria</i> (literally, "the illumination"), when torches and bonfires lit up the early summer night of 29 June.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A national feast since the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights</a>, Mnarja is a traditional Maltese festival of food, religion and music. The festivities still commence today with the reading of the <i>"bandu"</i>, an official governmental announcement, which has been read on this day in Malta since the 16th century. Originally, Mnarja was celebrated outside St. Paul's Grotto, in the north of Malta. However, by 1613 the focus of the festivities had shifted to the Cathedral of <a href="/wiki/Paul_of_Tarsus" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul of Tarsus">St. Paul</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Mdina" title="Mdina">Mdina</a>, and featured torchlight processions, the firing of 100 petards, horseraces, and races for men, boys and slaves. Modern Mnarja festivals take place in and around the woodlands of <a href="/wiki/Buskett" class="mw-redirect" title="Buskett">Buskett</a>, just outside the town of <a href="/wiki/Rabat_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="Rabat Malta">Rabat</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>It is said that under the Knights, this was the one day in the year when the Maltese were allowed to hunt and eat <a href="/wiki/Hare" title="Hare">wild rabbit</a>, which was otherwise reserved for the hunting pleasures of the Knights. The close connection between Mnarja and <a href="/wiki/Rabbit_stew" title="Rabbit stew">rabbit stew</a> (Maltese: <i>"fenkata"</i>) remains strong today.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1854 British governor <a href="/wiki/William_Reid_(British_Army_officer)" title="William Reid (British Army officer)">William Reid</a> launched an agricultural show at Buskett which is still being held today. The farmers' exhibition is still a seminal part of the Mnarja festivities today.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Mnarja today is one of the few occasions when participants may hear traditional Maltese "<a href="/wiki/G%C4%A7ana" class="mw-redirect" title="Għana">għana</a>". Traditionally, grooms would promise to take their brides to Mnarja during the first year of marriage. For luck, many of the brides would attend in their wedding gown and veil, although this custom has long since disappeared from the islands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Isle of MTV is a one-day music festival produced and broadcast on an annual basis by MTV. The festival has been arranged annually in Malta since 2007, with major pop artists performing each year. 2012 saw the performances of worldwide acclaimed artists Flo Rida, Nelly Furtado and Will.I.Am at Fosos Square in Floriana. Over 50,000 people attended, which marked the biggest attendance so far.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009 the first New Year's Eve street party was organised in Malta, parallel to what major countries in the world organise. Although the event was not highly advertised, and was controversial due to the closing of an arterial street on the day, it is deemed to have been successful and will most likely be organised every year.
</p><p>The Malta International Fireworks Festival is an annual festival that has been arranged in the Grand Harbour of Valletta since 2003. The festival offers fireworks displays of a number of Maltese as well as foreign fireworks factories. The festival is usually held in the last week of April every year.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Malta&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Malta" title="List of newspapers in Malta">List of newspapers in Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Malta" title="List of radio stations in Malta">List of radio stations in Malta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Malta" title="Television in Malta">Television in Malta</a></div>
<p>The most widely read and financially the strongest newspapers are published by Allied Newspapers Ltd., mainly <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_of_Malta" class="mw-redirect" title="The Times of Malta">The Times of Malta</a></i> (27 per cent) and its Sunday edition <i>The Sunday Times of Malta</i> (51.6 per cent).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Due to <a href="/wiki/Bilingualism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingualism">bilingualism</a> half of the newspapers are published in English and the other half in <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>. The Sunday newspaper <i>It-Torċa</i> ("The Torch") published by the Union Press, a subsidiary of the <a href="/wiki/General_Workers%27_Union_(Malta)" title="General Workers&#39; Union (Malta)">General Workers' Union</a>, is the widest Maltese language paper. Its sister paper, <i><a href="/wiki/L-Orizzont" title="L-Orizzont">L-Orizzont</a></i> ("The Horizon"), is the Maltese daily with biggest circulation. There is a high number of daily or weekly newspapers; there is one paper for every 28,000&#160;people. Advertising, sales and <a href="/wiki/Subsidies" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsidies">subsidies</a> are the three main methods of financing newspapers and magazines. However, most of the papers and magazines tied to institutions are subsidised by the same institutions, they depend on advertising or subsidies from their owners.<sup id="cite_ref-a1_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-a1-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are eight terrestrial television channels in Malta: <a href="/wiki/TVM_(Malta)" class="mw-redirect" title="TVM (Malta)">TVM</a>, <a href="/wiki/TVM2" title="TVM2">TVM2</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliament_TV_(Malta)" title="Parliament TV (Malta)">Parliament TV</a>, <a href="/wiki/One_(Maltese_TV_channel)" title="One (Maltese TV channel)">One</a>, <a href="/wiki/NET_Television_(Malta)" class="mw-redirect" title="NET Television (Malta)">NET Television</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smash_Television" title="Smash Television">Smash Television</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=F_Living&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="F Living (page does not exist)">F Living</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xejk" title="Xejk">Xejk</a>. These channels are transmitted by digital terrestrial, free-to-air signals on <a href="/wiki/Ultra_high_frequency" title="Ultra high frequency">UHF</a> channel 66.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> The state and <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Malta" title="List of political parties in Malta">political parties</a> subsidise most of the funding of these television stations. TVM, TVM2 and Parliament TV are operated by <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Services" title="Public Broadcasting Services">Public Broadcasting Services</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Public_broadcasting" title="Public broadcasting">national broadcaster</a> and member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">EBU</a>. Media.link Communications Ltd., the owner of NET Television, and <a href="/wiki/One_Productions_Ltd" class="mw-redirect" title="One Productions Ltd">One Productions Ltd</a>., the owner of One, are affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Party_(Malta)" title="Nationalist Party (Malta)">Nationalist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(Malta)" title="Labour Party (Malta)">Labour</a> parties, respectively. The rest are privately owned. The Malta Broadcasting Authority supervises all local broadcasting stations and ensures their compliance with legal and licence obligations as well as the preservation of due impartiality; in respect of matters of political or industrial controversy or relating to current public policy; while fairly apportioning broadcasting facilities and time between persons belong to different political parties. The Broadcasting Authority ensures that local broadcasting services consist of public, private and community broadcasts that offer varied and comprehensive programming to cater for all interests and tastes.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Malta Communications Authority reported that there were 147,896 pay TV subscriptions active at the end of 2012, which includes analogue and digital cable, pay digital terrestrial TV and IPTV.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> For reference the latest census counts 139,583 households in Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> Satellite reception is available to receive other European television networks such as the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> from Great Britain and <a href="/wiki/RAI" title="RAI">RAI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mediaset" title="Mediaset">Mediaset</a> from Italy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-ReferenceA-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ReferenceA_42-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.timesofmalta.com/articles/view/20140914/local/So-who-are-the-real-Maltese-.535578"><i>So who are the 'real' Maltese</i></a>. <q>There's a gap between 800 and 1200 where there is no record of civilisation. It doesn't mean the place was completely uninhabited. There may have been a few people living here and there, but not much……..The Arab influence on the Maltese language is not a result of Arab rule in Malta, Prof. Felice said. The influence is probably indirect, since the Arabs raided the island and left no-one behind, except for a few people. There are no records of civilisation of any kind at the time. The kind of Arabic used in the Maltese language is most likely derived from the language spoken by those that repopulated the island from Sicily in the early second millennium; it is known as Siculo-Arab.  The Maltese are mostly descendants of these people.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=So+who+are+the+%27real%27+Maltese&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.timesofmalta.com%2Farticles%2Fview%2F20140914%2Flocal%2FSo-who-are-the-real-Maltese-.535578&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMalta" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><i>The origin of the Maltese surnames</i>. <q>Ibn Khaldun puts the expulsion of Islam from the Maltese Islands to the year 1249. It is not clear what actually happened then, except that the Maltese language, derived from Arabic, certainly survived. Either the number of Christians was far larger than Giliberto had indicated, and they themselves already spoke Maltese, or a large proportion of the Muslims themselves accepted baptism and stayed behind. Henri Bresc has written that there are indications of further Muslim political activity on Malta during the last Suabian years. Anyhow there is no doubt that by the beginning of Angevin times no professed Muslim Maltese remained either as free persons or even as serfs on the island.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+origin+of+the+Maltese+surnames&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMalta" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r861714446"/></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
<a href="/wiki/Robert_Montgomery_Martin" title="Robert Montgomery Martin">Martin, Robert Montgomery</a> (1843). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=yDQGAAAAMAAJ&amp;pg=RA1-PA568"><i>History of the colonies of the British Empire</i></a>, W. H. Allen, p. 569: "Malta remained for 72 years subject of the emperors of Germany. The island was after the period of Count Roger of the Normans afterwards given up to the Germans, on account of the marriage between Constance, heiress of Sicily, and Henry VI, son of the Emperor Friedrick Barbarossa. Malta was elevated to a county and a marquisate, but its trade was now totally ruined, and for a considerable period of it remained solely a fortified garrison."</span>
